--- 帖子 #1 ---
like most people ive made money lost money always lookin for somethin that works bla bla blaaaaa were all really tired of talkin about that arent we?

well finally "found" somethin its actually the slingshot system by buffy or i think its called "bline" and i made my own version which is slightly a bit different from his template.

this works on any timeframe really. but i prefer either scalping it on the 5 min or 15 or 1h maybe 4h.

money management? thats up to u. my stops are discretionary and i look at previous highs or go for 10-15 pips if im trading 5min or 15 min it really depends on alot of stuff. but im sorry i cant help u there since ive done very well on counting on my experience when it comes to stops. same with targets. at least aim for the same as the stop u use. plus this system was made for nasdaq and SnP and its deff different from fxxxxxxx.

but this is not gonna be too worrying because im only gonna write and show the best trades. no reason to over trade and no reason to enter a half assed trade or one ur not too sure off. only look for the best best trades so that ur stop can be tight and u can secure an easy 25-30 pips a day on the 5 or 15 min. i can almost assure u theres a perfect trade everyday.

the setup:

stochastics:

k:20

d:10

slowing:20

another stochastics in the same window. this one is longer term.

k:50

d:10

slowing:20

3rd stochastics in the same window. this one is for entry.

k:5

d:3

slowing:3

first indication: what u need to do is first look at the 20 and the 50 and see what they are doing. this is not necessary but when the 20 is above the 50 then thats my first hint the trend is up

when the 20 is below the 50 then trend is down.

sometimes they are really close to each other which should make u cautious about taking trades.

second indication: you want the 20 to be crossed down with its signal line and the 50 to be doing the same. if both are crossed down with their signal lines then price is trending down and we look to sell.

vice versa for when they are crossed up.

taking trades: when the 20 and the 50 have crossed their signal lines down we look at the 5. we want the 5 to go into overbought if the trend is down. basically we are looking for a pullback. as soon as the 5 cross back down we enter. if a nice tiny little consolidation formed and 20 and 50 are trending down and nicely then enter at that even if the 5 didnt make it very high.

vice versa when the 20 and 50 are trending up

the examples will clear up everything and ill be posting a  few after im done with this post but im gonna add some remarks and then attach the first image.

remarks:

- the cross of the 20 and 50 is not so reliable. like an MA cross it can be tricky. but its good to look at because it can keep u away from bad trades.

- when the 20 cross its signal line, look at how steep its going up or down and also look at the space between the main line and the signal. the bigger the space the better the trade will be. same with the slope the steeper it is the better. this is stuff that after a few live and posted examples u will learn to see for yourself and ull know when its nice and trendy and when its being naughty.

- the 5 doesnt have to pull back all the way into oversold or overbought area. wait for a consolidation of price or for stochs to cross then enter. in a strong trend u can easily see when price stalls before continuing.

- im awesome

- if i can think of anything else ill deff add.

- o yea.

perfect long trade:

20 cross the 50 up.

20 and 50 both crossed their signal line up and are slopped nicely

5 pulls back all the way into oversold while price is stalling and consolidating.

- also try adding a 9 ema and a 34 ema (i like the fibo numbers) and when ur about to take a trade check if the 9 crossed the 34 up if ur taking a long trade or down if its a short. this is really just extra confirmation. i dont personally use it unless im really really bored.

ok. u know feel free to add anything and i dont take all the credit but a bit of it for my variations.

ok first chart

the 20 is crossed up with the 50. they have both crossed their signal lines and are moving up nicely. the 5 didnt go all the way down but price consolidated. i would enter at the bar right after the one with the low. basically telling me price isnt going any lower. i wait for it to close then i enter. this is a bit discretionary but thats how i do things. i look for little confirmations. another one is that star looking bar with the low. it has a name the open is the same as the close and it shows indecision so thats another small confirmation..

ok more to come next. stay tuned

--- 帖子 #18 ---
I notice in the chart of post #8 that you have a structure which I call a "bundling" of stochastics.  While I do not use these structures in my system I have noticed these while I was working on the combination of  indicators for my system.  What I had observed is that these are high probability reversal trades.  I was wondering whether you use these as entries.

I realize that in your system the 20 and 50 would have to be heading up at the time for you to take the trade, and when these structures happen they would not be heading either up or down, since by definition they would have to be neutral since they are at the point of turning.  You might consider using these structures as triggers for your entries.  Anyway, you might want to watch them and see whether this type of entry would suit your system.

One thing I really like about your system is that you have a low failure rate and this is something which I have worked very hard to build into my system, although I tend to be looking for a larger number of pips per trade, usually 20 or more.  I consider minimizing losses more important than maximizing wins.  It is easy to find winning trades, it is much harder to avoid losers.  How many newbies have made large amounts on good trades only to see all of it and more get lost on the bad ones?

--- 帖子 #35 ---
I am enclosing a chart of a particularly good set of 3 examples of what I am talking about.  It is the 1H Swissie chart.  The first 2 bundles are in overbought territory, the third is not.  Look carefully for the second bundle because the arrow is in the printing at the top of the chart.

I would have taken the first 2 trades in overbought territory and not the third which was midrange.  You will also see that the first 2 would have succeeded and the third not.

I do not know if you have ever noticed any of my posts, but I am a fan of looking at multiple timeframes using the same indicator(s) in my trading system.  I apply the same rule to others.

I have found that different timeframes work best for different pairs.  I usually use 3 timeframes, but only 2 for some pairs.  I advise everyone to experiment with this.   You will find that it keeps you out of an amazing number of bad trades.  Do not worry about the good trades it also keeps you out of because the bad trades you do not take more than make up for this.

--- 帖子 #36 ---
ur time is limited and can only watch long term charts? well i gotta solution for you.

1: 20 and 50 are trending down nicely. big spread between the 20 and its signal line same with the 50. 100 is also trending down. the 5 pulls back pretty far almost into overbought area. enter at the cross of the 5 stochs when the new candle opens.stop above the previous days high its the bar with the x above it and target usually more than the stop. in this case sell at 1.2486 stop at 2552 target at 2386. the stop is 66 i would target a bit more than the stop and go for 100.

2: same story. stop is around 100 pips so target 150-200 MINIMUM. which u can obviously see it made 400-500 pips. in a case like that i would get out 40-50% of my position at 100 pips profit move my stop to breakeven and aim for another 100 pips. if thats easily reached then ill close a bit more of my position and move my stop to 100 pips then aim for another 50 or 100. that way u can get the most bang for ur $$$$.

3: why take this one? the 5 barely  pulled back. but a continuation from 2 this would be a great confirmation that price is falling even more so that u know u can catch some more profit

4: tricky because 100 is oversold and flat. all indications show for a good trade but since the 100 is flat and oversold and were lookin to buy then it would have made me careful. i would have probably taken the trade with a smaller stop than the previous low and a target of about the same.

5: perfect trade. once the big bar closes enter when the next bar opens with a stop at the big bar's low. target around 1.5 to 2 times the stop or do like i described in trade #2

6: very nice trade in the making. 20 overbought and above its signal line. 50 and 100 trending up nicely. the 5 already half way. i would wait for a cross of the 5 up and enter. keep ur eyes open for this one as long as the cross of the 5 happens and everything else agrees then were in business baby!!!.

--- 帖子 #64 ---
Here are three nice trades on the GBP/USD pair today. Could have gotten you over 100pips.

When I use this method on the 15minute charts, I like to wait for the close of the candle. And most importantly, I like the candle to be a reversal type. Example: hammer, doji, spinning top, etc...

Trade 1: Buy, 20 and 50 were trending up, 5 retraced halfway and a Doji formed. Here's a situation when the 20 was below the 50, but since they were trending up it was still a good trade.

Trade 2: Sell, 20 and 50 were below their signal lines and trending down, 5 retraced halfway, consolidation formed, 2 Hammers formed. Perfect trade setup.

Trade 3: Sell, 20 and 50 were still below their signal lines and trending down at a nice angle, 5 retraced a little, consolidation formed, Hammer/Doji formed. ( you could have waited until the second time the 5 retraced and a bigger hammer formed around 1800GMT)  ***This trade is near the US session ending, activity is slowing down and you'd probably only want to get 10 or 15pips***

--- 帖子 #82 ---
Hi FJFX,

Regarding the 5 crossing it's own signal line, I don't wait for a cross.  I just wait for the 5 to pull back into the neutral area or better yet(if it happens) the oversold/overbought area.

Personally, I myself need a few good reasons to enter a trade...not just one.  Not sure I can explain my thought process because it's different each time depending on the trade setup and time of day.  As with my exit strategies.  During the Asian session or towards the end of the US session...I'm only looking for 10-15pip gains because there isn't much action.  During the London Open through London Close you get much more action so I try to get anywhere from 25-50pips.  It all depends on what I see setting up on the charts...and the candle formations.  If I see hammers, doji's, railroad track, etc.  Then I go ahead and take my profits then usually because a reversal could be coming up.   I think the main thing is to enter GOOD trades and MINIMIZE your losses!  Get that under control and the rest will fall into place.

Goodluck!

--- 帖子 #111 ---
What I said is quite correct: I do not enter a trade until the 5 has crossed and headed in the direction of the trade.

What I should have added, was that I trade GBP/JPY frequently and have again and again seen this pair bounce up to 120 pips.  That makes it more important to wait with this pair than most others.  Generally, the more volatile the pair the more important it is to wait for the 5.  I do not like to have to put stops larger than 80 to 100 pips, and I rarely like stops that large except in position trades.

One of the risks here is that there was news coming out which could affect this pair.  Generally the news which came out an hour and a half ago  was yen negative, which would have the effect of raising the price of the pair or at least supporting it.  In addition there is AM US news (durable goods and new homes) which can affect cable and if it does, cable could drag this pair along with it.  Moves from news tend to be short duration and rarely make lasting changes in the direction of a pair, but on the short term can have a large effect.

These are the reasons why I have held off on the entry and will continue waiting until and unless a clear change in the slope of the 5 occurs.  This will limit the drawdown to that which would be caused by news alone, rather than be additive of the effect of the bounce plus potentially the effect of news.

< What am I doing wrong? When I use the MTF Stoch it produces a 20 and 80 level for each pair of lines (top). How do I get it to look like the "regular" Stoch (bottom) >

Looks like you need to adjust the Minimum and Maximum value of the indicator(s) . Open the properties window of the indicator and select the Common tab , check and adjust the Fixed minimum and Fixed maximum amounts .

--- 帖子 #136 ---
Boxing, for whatever my opinion is worth, I just wanted to say that I think you've got a very sound system here – although I guess you already know that!    Yours is one of the methods that I'm looking to trial over the next few months. Haven't finalized my timeframe(s) yet.

IMHO entering on the resumption of a strong trend following a decent pullback (and vice versa for a short position) is arguably the safest setup. It means (1) entering a trend at a decent price (improves R/R), and (2) with the added insurance that if the market happens to switch from "trending" to "ranging" mode, then you're still likely to catch something near the bottom of the range (for a long trade).

Every successful TA-based entry method I've ever seen ultimately breaks down to one of two methods: trend-based pullbacks, or breakouts. The rest is semantics regarding timing.

I'm generally not a fan of indicators, but IMHO stochastics and Bollinger bands are the among the very best for measuring overbought/oversold.

A few more things I've noticed, although I'm probably re-stating the obvious…..

As the 20 and 50 rise from oversold, that's generally the first impulse wave (Elliott wave #1) in the new trend. The pullback is the first retracement (akin to E wave #2) and the resumption (where 20 and 50 are rising and 5 crosses above its signal) is the second impulse wave (E wave #3, proceeding from the second shoulder in an inverted H&S), which is frequently the largest move in the trend. Your multi leveled stochastics are confirming this price action.

If the trend is prolonged, then it's still possible to trade pullbacks while 20 and 50 remain in overbought territory, as these are subsequent waves in the uptrend. However, I suspect that the probability of success diminishes a little with each successive pullback. Also, I suspect that risk increases if the entry bar is tall (if you wait for it to complete before entering) and/or takes price into an area of prior resistance.

As well as using some price action patterns to help with entry, you could probably also use horizontals (prior support/resistance, Fibos, pivot levels, etc) for confirmation, and (perhaps) also to scale out for profit. These are some of the variations I hope to test. I also like to see price in relation to Bollinger bands, using the channel width to confirm the R/R potential of a candidate trade.

If trading the H1 or longer, one could also drill down to the shorter timeframes for help with timing of entry.

Anyway, for whatever my opinion is worth, this is a great method. Well done!

And I hope and pray for your continued safety in Beirut.

Best wishes

David

well when the 5 pulls back watch price to pull back a bit and consolidate if it does and the 20 and 50 are still trending down then trend is still down. now no system is perfect so lets say u went short and price broke above then it was a bad signal and it happens but they are rare and as long as the main things are confirming the trade then take it. there is no way of knowing but most of the times when the 5 pulls back adn price breaks pretty high then trend is reversing also watch the 20 and 50 if that happens they usually  change direction too. also about last night i dont see any tricky or bad signals on the 1h gbpusd or the 15 min

if u want post a chart and draw a circle on the area ur talking about that way i can explain more.

about timeframes theres no ideal timeframe. each has its own characteristics and what not. last week i took 2 or 3 trades off the 4h chart all winners. yesterday 2 trades off the 15 min gbpusd each good for 15-25 pips. there was also a short gbpusd 1h yesterday good for near 100 pips or so. each timeframe has its own stops and targets and all this stuff. it can depend on ur availability. if ur available around volatile times for a while then trade off the 15 min unless theres a nice 1h signal. if u can periodically check then the 1h chart should give nice trades pretty often. it also depends on the pair. dont trade a pair with a 15 pip spread off the 5 min chart. tahts just asking to lose money. and dont trade the euro for example off the 5 or 15 min during the asian session. ur chances of that trade making pips is very low. so it really depends on all this stuff and i cant actually tell u what to do and when and what to trade coz one thing might work for me but not u but in the end u can make all timeframes work and any pair. i suggest u start with 15 min and 1h and if u dont ahve alot of time study the 1h and 4h charts.

as for contradicting signals on different time frames, dont confuse urself with too many timeframes. if ur unsure just dont trade simple as that. its what i do. just because the 15 is pointing down but the 1h is pointing up doesnt mean one is gonna win. the price could go down according to 15 then go up. remember different time frames are different timeframes and they will contradict each other sometimes. also try not to look at a 5 min chart then a 4h chart for confirmation lol thats just silly. for 15 min try confirming with 1h and for 1h try confirming with 4h. also trading the 5 min chart can be rewarding i consider it advanced and dont look at it too much. too many false signals.

i hope this helps everybody. people keep it simple trust me dont look into it too much  theres nothin perfect if the trade fails it fails even the best traders will have bad trades it happens.

--- 帖子 #200 ---
my sequence:

i glance at the 4h to see what its doing. trend is up then im biased to go long when its the right time on the other time frames. lets say trend is up. i then look at the 1h and 15 min. lets say 1h is trending down. to me this is a retracement and the move down will be small and short lived and then price will consolidate. if everything is as planned the 15 would have turned up and the 1h would be trending down slightly but with more signs of being flat or the 50 is flat for example. then ill start taking trades off the 15 min if its an active time of day and when the first signal works the 1h should be turning up then ill look for more signals on teh 15 min and 1h. this will get easier with practice and experience. ur question is a smart one but it made my head spin and to me for no reason. keep it simple. bad trades will happen and there is no way to avoid them 100%. ive had a bad trade last night. it wasnt a system trade but i was just bored to be honest and lost 30 pips. im over it coz i know theyl happen even though i could have avoid it. i can say with lots of proudness that taking the best setups u will have at least 8 out of 10 trades to be winners.

4h: main trend

1h: watch for retracements from a 4h move or for price consolidation that are saying 4h trend is good and the 1h has just retraced and it isnt moving against the 4h any further

15 min: following teh 4h. look for first trade during active time. if things go smooth, the 1h will follow then things should be smooth sailing from there

hope this helps a bit

HI THERE BOXINGISLIFE

in direct answer to your question, i have taken your strategy , and put it along with another indicator "directional movement adx" . this gives volume indication .

the opportunity of catching a trend in the making is best when the adx line has reset itself by going under a reading of 20 (however, gbp usd is more reliable to just dip under . some other pairs do not dip below before heading back up again) , and then waiting for it to break out again. then using YOUR stochastic 5;3;3 for a pullback entry . (you can put this stoch on the adx as well) also the 9 &34 moving average could be on the main part of the chart for another visual confirmation of a breakout

i colour my di positive and negative lines green and red for easy understanding . admittedly , i do not trade anything less than 30min charts . my fave is 2hr . so the perfect scenario would be waiting for the adx to break out from below 20, and the 9 &34 moving averages to cross as well .then wait for stoch 5.3.3 to register a pullback

to jump in .your exit points could either be when that stoch crosses back again , or when the adx line starts to head back down (a few more pips for your money!!!!!). but sometimes even then , you miss out on quite a few pips because it still carries on after the adx is heading down . so you could leave the exit until price crosses back a few pips over the 34 moving ave . the choice of risk is yours . you will get better results when adx is heading up , rather than heading down

p.s i would post a chart , but my computer has internal issues at the moment

which i am trying to rectify asap.

--- 帖子 #229 ---
Firstly, boxingislife thanks for sharing a very powerful trading plan.

For my first post at ForexFactory I have made an indicator to assist those using this method.

It is an alarm. When the quickest stochastic changes to a new trend which agrees with both the longer stochs an alarm will sound. The alarm should sound each tick for the period of the candle so long as the conditions are still met.

With the default settings the alarm only works when the fastest stoch:

1. Candle 0(the candle being formed) is indicating a new trend

2. Candle 1(the last complete candle) is indicating a new trend(the crossover)

3. Candle 2(the 2nd last complete candle) is indicating the old trend

When the alarm sounds a check of the expert box in the terminal window will indicate which currency, timeframe and direction is alarming.

Any problems with it please let me know. I don't proffess to be a coder but I am willing to give it a go.

Short of an ea I think this alarm will help an already solid approach.

--- 帖子 #230 ---
I have got 5 charts per currency set up, from 5m to 4H, using two currencies.  Anyway the constant alarms are driving me crazy.  I already had the option to turn the alarm off but now I have included a print function.  Otherwise if an alarm goes off and I don't like the look of the setup I can turn the alarm off that particular time frame and currency.  But it gets hard to keep track which chart has the alarm turned off or on.

So now it will let you know if the alarm is off in the terminal expert section.

This is an indicator not an expert.

- the 4h is ranging. so to me that says no true direction. when that happens i automatically switch to the 1h chart because theres always trends. since the 4h is ranging well its goin up and down so its trending except the only way to see that trend is a faster timeframe. so we go to the 1h.

- 1h its been going up just by lookin at price. well yesterday the 20 and 50 started trending down. so price dropped and consolidated and it retraced. if u draw some fibos u see price went to around the 50% mark and stalled. at the same time u had a great short trade forming . there you go you would have taken that trade and come out a winner.

--- 帖子 #263 ---
pipette4x glad u like it and if u have any questions please feel free to ask

ahil

im really not a big fan of expert advisors for alot of reason. i dont believe in making money while doing nothing unless ive worked and done somethin for 30-40 years and im retiring and making money off some investment or something

this system has alot of discretion involved. the more ur successful at it the more you filter out the average/good trades from the perfect trades even if they bring alot of pips. a expert advisor can trade according to parameters but doesnt have and would never have the logic that humans have after experience.

another thing is timeframes. while there can be a great trade on the 1h, a quick signal on the 15 min against the 1h that is enough to trigger a trade would lose some hard earned pips. also u cant just put it on 1h coz then ull be missing alot of trades on the 15 min and even the 5 min

i personally cannot come home to the fact that for example my expert advisor lost money today while i could have made money or the target was missed by 1 pip then the stop was hit or whatever the case is. u can blame it all u want but in the end its like using a signal service. its ur fault for trusting it while u could have traded it urself and made money.

i can list a few more reasons but all im saying is im not a fan of expert advisors nor would i support them on my thread. no hard feelings just the way i like to do things

learn to trade the system and ull get to a point where ull enjoy trading

--- 帖子 #277 ---
I realize changing a system before you've actually traded it a month or so is kind of taboo but I had to mold this to better fit my time frame and personality.  It also happens that this works out fairly well..

I only have the 50,10,20 on my charts.  Specifically the 1hr cable and swiss.  I go short when the main line has gone above overbought (80) and drops back down again.  Likewise I go long when the main line drops below oversold (20) and pops back up again.

Exit either at the next sell signal, a predefined stop loss or when the main line crosses the trigger line (but ONLY if they are both between the 80 and 20 levels - crosses of the main/trigger are ignored when in overbought and oversold areas).

I have also added a tunnel to the chart, using the 62 EMA w/ +10 and -10 levels on it.  This can be used in one of two ways.  When a currency is trending hard, a slight retracement might actually cause the stochastics to drop below (or above) the over/under sold line indicating a new position.  In this case, I use the tunnel as confirmation of entry.  If the price does not cross the tunnel I do not take the trade.  Again, I typically only use this tunnel in cases of trending markets.   The second use would be to always use the tunnel as added confirmation of a trade - many times the price will range within the tunnel before continuing on in the direction of the stoch signal.  Up to you.

Jason

--- 帖子 #292 ---
But only one logic problem here:

The signal on the 5 min and 15 min chart will ALWAYS come first as the 1H bar is build AFTER 4 of 15 min or 12 of 5 min bars are created.

So, if we wait for the 1H bar it may be too late for the short term trade of the 5/15M chart. But, the signal on 5 or 15 min may get us in the hourly trades earlier.

So Boxing, your input of resolving this issue is needed here, how do you deal with it in your call if to take the trade on a short TF or wait for the 1H bar to close first?

Tzachi

--- 帖子 #294 ---
ok one thing i think i should advise you guys to do is forget the 5 min chart. its too fast and its not a good idea to trade with it. use a 15 min chart if u want a small timeframe.

the way i do things is the following:

i look at the daily or 4h for a general idea. just a quick glance. lets say trend is up.

i open my 1h chart and check the 20 and 50 lets say they are flat and its early in the euro. session but action is starting to pick up. so i take a look at my 15 min and i see a nice 20 and 50 trending up and the 5 pulling back with price making a small move up and then consolidating.  i take teh trade. lets say it went up 15-20-30 pips whatever. i get out at some point then check to see if the 20 and 50 are still trending.  and i check the 1h.

i like to keep things simple and prefer taking trades off higher tameframes rather than the smaller ones but il  go to smaller timeframes when the higher ones are not showing any signals.

so for example if i check the 1h and its trending up with the 5 pulling back then i forget the 15 min and i look to buy when price consolidates because signals on teh 1h are much safer to trade. if its trending up but the 5 is already overbought or acting funny then i go to the 15 min and check for trades. or if the 1h is trending up and finished a first signal or during a trade i check the 15 for opportunities and add to my trade on a very tiny pull back. it can be many things. but the 1h and 15 min are close so they shouldn confuse u. and guys trade take alot of trades especially on the demo. the losers will teach u what u did wrong and how it can be avoided.

hope this clears up some issues

--- 帖子 #371 ---
Actually I use all time frames from 5M to daily, but most often the 15M, 30M, 1H and 4H charts.

I do not like to trade unless I have 2 adjacenty time frames which agree, or at least do not conflict.  I will trade with a good set up on one time frame and a neutral on an adjacent time frame.  Usually I use 15M and 30M together, 1H and 4H together.

I use the 5M for scalping and always to help with the most advantageous entry to a trade which I had a set up for on another time frame.  I just use the slow stochastic on the 5M for these purposes.

In those rare cases in which there are 3 or more charts which all agree on a trade, I increase my trade size.  This does not occur often.

I hope this helps because when I follow my rules absolutely to the letter, I may have some breakeven trades but few if any losses.

--- 帖子 #377 ---
I suspect that I do not like to leave pips on the table any more than you do, but I have learned that more often than not in trying to get every pip, I ended up with fewer pips rather than more.  So now, as long as I get pips in a trade, I am happy.  Of course, more is better, but any are nice--and certainly better than losing some.

As to exiting trades, I find that if I use the 5 cross on the 5M chart, I leave very few pips behind.  The shorter the time frame I use the 5 on, the better my entries and exits.  I find 1M charts too hard to work with, but 5M charts leave very few pips behind.  Unless I am scalping I only use the 5M for entries, and exits.  And I have to be incredibly desperate or incredibly bored to scalp since it is not a way I like to trade.

In your honor, I've created an indicator.

Attach it to a chart, then click through the different timeframes, and if conditions are set up in that timeframe, it will give the alert.

It will give an short alert when:

50 stoch is below the signal line

20 stoch is below the signal line

5 stoch is above 60

Gives long alert when:

50 is above signal

20 is above signal

5 is below 40

It will only give the alert one time per bar.

Hope you all can use this on this great strategy. If you don't like the 40 and 60 levels, it's easy to edit. I've given the source code, and the numbers 40 and 60 are only used once in there, just go in and change them.

Also attached my template.

Hello,

In order to get familiar with the system and find a method to stick to the rules I developed a matrix in which I can judge the phase of each timeframe.

From that I try to say what signals I should be looking for in a certain time frame. Then when I think a signal occurs I have to fill a blank sheet to be sure all criteria are met to enter a position in the particular time frame. Working this way I hope to eliminate entering trades because I think I see something or because I think something will happen. Like I read somewhere: "Trade what you see, not what you think".

I enclosed the sheet and will let you know within the coming weeks wether it works for me. Feel free to use it also or comment on it.

--- 帖子 #399 ---
I think that everyone has had problems (or is having problems) with chasing the market.  The question always comes down to how late is too late?  No real answer to that one.  This problem usually arises when there has been a 'dry' period with no really good trades to take.  Then there is a tendency to jump at a trade which is borderline rather than really good.  Trades tend to come in bunches, lots of good ones at once or only bad ones.

It does require patience and discipline.  I still sometimes violate my own rules for what appear at the time to be good reasons, but in retrospect were clearly not.  I often wonder at my decisions at those times.

The most important things to put up in large letters on the wall for me are:

1. follow the rules, follow the rules, follow the rules

2. it is more important to avoid a losing trade than to miss a winning trade

3. there will always be other good trades

These are the things I keep trying to remind myself of.  As long as I do those 3 things, I usually to great.  When I violate them, then well......

It does take patience, and remember that trades are winners or losers based on your time frame and drawdown tolerance.  You can trade the micro movements (scalping), the short term movements of 10 to 50 pips, the medium term movements of 50 to 100 pips or the long term movements of 100+ pips.  As in all matters, the greater the potential reward the greater the potential risk, therefore if you are willing to weather substantial drawdown (what would be losing trades for people trading shorter time frames) you can have winners for substantial pips when most are losing.

Personally I lack the patience for position trades.  I prefer day trading.  I rarely get more than 100 pips from a trade, but I also do not need huge stop losses, and if I follow my rules strictly I rarely have losses.

I do not know whether any of this will help you, I hope so.  These are things I think about all the time and try to keep reminding myself of.

--- 帖子 #421 ---
My last post was for the purpose of demonstrating the risks of using just one chart to determine the direction of a trade.  In this case, there were good looking setups for trades in both directions, and the best looking showed a trade in a direction contrary to the move which started shortly thereafter.  If you consistently look for 2 adjacent time frames which show consistent trades or at least one showing a good trade and the other neutral, you have a much higher probability trade.

--- 帖子 #453 ---
First, I need to have 2 time frames which agree, preferably adjacent ones, but if I have 1 very good looking chart I will accept the adjacent one being neutral.  I do not concern myself with other time frames at that point.

You can have a long trade which you plan to hold to 1 to 2 hours, and at the same time have a short trade which you intend to hold for a day and have both of them close with a profit.

As you know what happens on the short term may have very little to do with what occurs on the long term.  Very occasionally you get a picture where all the charts are going in the same direction.  That is worth its weight in gold because it is a virtual guarantee of success, unfortunately this happens very rarely.

If I am planning a medium to long term trade I do not concern myself overly with the short time frames except to use for my entry.  With short term trades the long term charts only tell my how "safe" my trade is which determines whether I stay in it for bounces or dips or exit each time, wait out the bounce or dip and get back in.

--- 帖子 #455 ---
It is clear.  I do not believe that Boxing uses multiple time frames, but I do.

No, I would not take a trade in which I had a matching signal on the 4H and 15M but with all the other time frames having opposite signals.  That is just my way of trading any signal.  I am happiest and most confident when I have more than 2 adjacent signals agreeing.

I have a custom indicator that I use for range trading in which I need a particular set of 3 time frames to agree for me to take a trade.  The 3 time frames are different for different pairs, and one pair I only use 2 time frames.  I have learned that no matter what indicators or system you use, if you use more than 1 time frame your chances of success are much higher.

--- 帖子 #472 ---
You see, I am retired and can do what I please when I please.  I am a dinosaur from pre-PC days and the most useful indicators for me are multiple stochastics in all markets and a combination of Rubber band and stochastics in ranging markets only.

It took me a while to get used to using indicators and even after I started learning about them, I ended up last fall for 2 months with a computer so ancient that it could not handle putting much on charts and would not even allow me to have more than one window open  at a time.  I could not have my email program open or FF at the same time as my platform and I could not even put the Rubber band indicator on the platform.  So I basically went back to the old way of trading and it was like the 80's revisited, but it still worked.  Even with a state of the art computer, I am still restricted by a dialup with connection speed usually between 24 and 26 (what can you expect when you live in a frozen wasteland?).  I look at most indicators and systems which get posted to FF and most of them I discard fairly rapidly, and I keep coming back to stochastics and Rubber band as the most reliable systems other than naked charts to trade.  But this is just what suits me and that does not mean that they are necessarily the best way for everyone to trade.

My past includes being a University instructor as well as being a physician.  If you are aware of the original intent of the term, you know that physicians were meant to be teachers, and that is how I saw my role (except when doing surgery).

What I have tried to do in this thread is to teach others in order for them to be able to avoid some of the very costly errors I have made.  One of the big differences between humans and animals is our ability to learn from the experience of others.

Trading is serious because it can result in the loss of serious amounts of money if you are trading a live account.  On the other hand, we must never lose our sense of humour or our ability to make fun of ourselves and what happens to us--we need to remain able to laugh at ourselves.  Please always feel free to have a laugh at my expense because I will join you.

--- 帖子 #479 ---
I can only tell you how I personally do things.  What I will say does not necessarily apply to the way anyone else uses multiple time frames.

I look for agreement between adjacent time frames.  Actually what I want to see is the 20 and 50 going in the same direction on both.  I will pay most attention to the direction of the 5 on the lower time frame.  If I have a very strong chart on one time frame and a neutral chart on the adjacent ones, then I may still trade the set up.  The ideal set up has all the stochs in agreement on 3 charts (yes, that really does happen sometimes) in which case I do not remember ever losing on the trade and I have learned to throw money management away when it does happen that way because I have learned that such set ups are as close to a guaranteed win as you will ever see in forex.

Remember that this is just my opinion and it is solely based on my own past experiences--no 2 people will look at the same charts and see quite the same thing.

--- 帖子 #480 ---
After rereading what I wrote, I realized that I should warn you of my personal biases.  The biggest one is that I REALLY do not like to lose trades and I will happily forgo winning trades in order to avoid losing ones.

Lately I have had only 1 trade (that is in quite a few weeks and I am a very active trader) which lost when I was following my trading rules.  The problem is that I need to learn to slap myself when I even consider a trade which does not follow my trading rules.  Still, I am up more than 70% during the past week.   I think I will have Mailboxes-are-us, or whatever they call themselves, print my trading rules up on a poster with letters 12 inches high.  That way I will not have the excuse of trading late at night without my glasses on and not being able to read them from a distance.  We all sometimes need to protect ourself from ourself.

At any rate, the more agreement you have between 2 charts the more likely the trade is to succeed and when you have virtually identical charts in 3 time frames you really have a winner.  Basically you want all of the stochastics heading in the same direction.

{Cable = GBP/USD because the Rate was originally  transported via the Transatlantic Copper Cable}

--- 帖子 #511 ---
I use NF so the operations may be different. In the table of indicators, when you select the Stochastic, don't just double click on it and make its settings. Instead highlight and drag it into the window with the other stoch.

Other indicators you may have to adjust the Apply To section to First Indicator. Though not with stoch.

Hope this helps you.

--- 帖子 #538 ---
Ok guys, i think i have definitely found the filter that suits boxingislife strategy.

NonlagMAV5 (V4 is approximatively the same so do not worry about the version) with the following settings :

0-9-0-3-1-0

Add Hama for trend following (this is really up to you but it definitely helps)

Looking to different timeframe does not help much in fact.

If you look each time frame on each currency pair, you will most of the time find one that give each signal necessary to take the good trade.

Signal are :

Perfect stochastic signal (look 1st post of boxingislife :X )

Nonlagma turns yellow with the next 2 or 3 candle or is allready on the right direction (red for downtrend - blue for uptrend )

hama bar turn to the right color (red downtrend, blue uptrend) This is optional but you have a 99% success rate with this signal added.

Side note : the smaller the TF, the longer you might wait for a confirming nonlagma signal (up to 4 candles on M5 )

I repeat, there is no need to watch a confirming TF. If the signal is perfect, it is indeed perfect for this time frame. Well i wont prevent you to watch to other TF, but i came to the conclusion that there is no constitent rule on watching other TF (sometime you need to look 2 TF ahead to have confirmation, sometime the next one, sometime none of them confirm the signal despite it perfectness, well you see the point )

One side note, nonlagma can sometime give a blue or red color despite the f(x)=1 (horizontal line, not sloppy)

In this case, the signal is not that good, wait for yellow (trend change) or sloppy nonlagma

I am trying to modify the source code on nonlagma so that no slope line would give another color but i have not success yet. If someone is good enough and has the time to modifiy it, it would be a nice visual improvement.

--- 帖子 #570 ---
I don't know if anyone's done this but it can be kind of fun. Cover up the main price window on your computer screen so that you can only see the indicator window. Now go back several months and looking only at the indicator window, decide what is a good buy signal and what is a good sell signal and mark the time of each one. Then after, go back and see if you were right or not. If nothing else, it'll make you analyze the indicator window harder and maybe find some new insights.

Currently I'm in testing of indicator based on this system. Do you have some canonical set of setups for entry/exit?

For example,

1) Stochs 20 and 50 should have one trend direction.

2) Stoch 5 should have and opposite trend direction to Stochs 20 and 50.

3) Stochs 20 and 50 should be in safe zone (not oversold or overbought)

4) Stochs 20 and 50 should have lag of 10 stoch's points (should not be too close to each other)

5) Stoch 5 should cross both Stochs 20 and 50

and so on.

I'll insert them into indicator, so everybody could select suitable set of setups. May be picture will help you to understand me

--- 帖子 #622 ---
Just one person's opinion, but I would be very careful about taking a short here.  I, personally, would not do it.

One reason is because there has been a fairly strong trend for the past 2 1/2 weeks, and this has been part of an overall bullish trend which began last summer, over 1000 pips ago.

A second reason is because your 20 and 50 are very flat with only a slight angle downward.

The third reason is that when I check the other time frames, none of the others shows a downward bias and most show a strong upward bias.

Given this situation, as far as I am concerned this is a low probability trade.

--- 帖子 #630 ---
You can usually get 20 to 60 pips from a good trade, sometimes more.

How many pips you average will depend on the quality of the set ups that you trade (the closer to the ideal that they are the greater the probability of success) and the longer the time frame that you use the greater the number of pips from a good trade.  Also, some days there seem to be quite a few good set ups and other days very few.

As with any system, even the best set ups will sometimes fail, so there are some losing trades, but if you are careful in your choice of trades, there are very few losses.

To get an idea, you might look at the trades that I posted and I usually added the result of the trade to the post or had to make a separate post with the results.  This should give you some idea of what to expect.

One trade I did not bother to post the results of was a GBP/JPY trade simply because I happen to get in on the start of a strong move with a set up on a short time frame.  The trade netted hundreds of pips.  Just luck in that case that a strong move was just starting.

--- 帖子 #673 ---
In general GBP/CHF and GBP/JPY move in similar ways, therefore if one is going down usually the other will also.  Since these pairs move about the same amount, there is no real advantage to trading one of them over the other.  The best idea with those 2 pairs is to pick the one you prefer and trade that one.  As for me, I happen to prefer GBP/JPY/

In the case of GBP/JPY and EUR/JPY, the reason for preferring to trade GBP/JPY is because it generally moves about 1/3 further on the moves.  In the current circumstance where cable and fiber are not moving parallel to each other the way they usually do, it is doubly preferable to trade GBP/JPY since the pound seems to be much weaker than the euro at the moment.

--- 帖子 #674 ---
Another option is to trade the one with the better swap... GBP/JPY has an horrible swap if you sell the pair, GPB/CHF is better ( near to 0 as the IR is 5% vs 5.5% )

--- 帖子 #705 ---
Hi Melpheos,

I do see some good trade signals on the 4H timeframe, but it seems like they take DAYS to setup.  However, that may work very well for some folks' trading style.

After analyzing the GBP/JPY and the USD/JPY over this weekend, I personally find the best quality signals to appear on the 30M charts for both pairs.  I'm going to be starting this week's trading with the following MO:

When I see a trade signal forming on 30M, I'll re-check against the higher TF charts (I always check the 1H and 4H charts at the beginning of trading anyway) to be sure the longer trends are in support of the 30M signal direction.  Then I'll zoom down to the 15M chart to get a closer look at the finer action and compare with the 30M chart as things move along.  When things have progressed to a possible entry point, I'll move down to the 5M chart to zero in my entry.

So, basically, I'll be using the 30M chart to identify the developing trade signals, verify them against the 1H/4H charts, then I'll move down to 15M and 5M to pull the trigger.  I've seen several trades that showed up very nicely on 30M, but if I had used the 30M chart to enter the trade, I would have missed a TON of pips due to late entry.

I have been reading another stochs trading thread in the Journal section by "Spudfyre".  His focus is on using a SINGLE stoch (the 5,3,3), but he puts it on multiple time-frames for the GBP/JPY.  Boxingislife's mutliple stochs method seems MUCH more favorable in terms of finding more and better entries, but Spudfyre's method reinforced in me the need to use multiple timeframes to help cherry pick the entries and manage the trades in process.

Well, enough rambling for now.  Hopefully, we'll ALL make some good pips this week using this VERY COOL system from Boxingislife!

--- 帖子 #720 ---
I don't really follow those pairs, but the signals look good to me.  I prefer a pullback of the 5,3,3 stoch which occurs clearly during the transition from OB to OS or OS to OB of the 20 and 50 stochs, which is what appears to be happening in both your pics.

When I see a signal forming on the higher TF's, such as 1H, I will zoom down to the 30M or 15M to dial in the entry a little closer.  If you make your entry based on the TF where you see the signal occur, you'll generally end up getting in a bit late because the 5 stoch line doesn't return to the direction of the 20/50 stochs until after the close of a full bar.

--- 帖子 #743 ---
Hello People

Firstly, good stuff Boxingislife for your enthusiasm and help to all the FX chickadees out there, I hope College and trading is going well for you.  This thread has gone a little quiet lately, which usually means one of two things, people cant make it work and are hunting for something easier or they are making bullion and dont need help anymore.  I hope it's the latter.

Personally, I love stochastics and have used them as my core methodology for over 6 years trading live.  Some great EA's have come out of it but the damn thing about stochastics is that you do need the human input and there are too many variables to program on what can be 'simply' gained by viewing the chart.  Ha! Simple.     After trading 20 hours a day for over 4 years its no wonder you start making an EA to lighten your load.

However, I digress.  This is a hard wearing methodology and will withstand anything thrown at it so carry it through and you will become very proficient just like Boxingislife.

I thought you all might enjoy some 'bells and whistles' to assist with not having to view the screen constantly.  Each of the indicators attached have the option of enabling a audible alarm which will activate once trend changes.  For those of you that are utilizing a Heiken Ashi as an additional filter, there is one that sits in it's own window like a stochastic (so it does not flood your chart) and the upside of this too is that you may wish to overlay your stochastics over the top.  For this reason I have attached 2 Heiken Ashi's, one with very light colors (Heiken Ashi LC) and the other darker shaded.

Furthermore, find attached the Moving Average Crossover indicator which also has the optional audible alert and even email alert.  I have hard coded the settings according to those whom follow the pdf notes Melpheos typed, so there is no need to input anything, simply attach to chart and all is set.

Heiken ashi requires that you set the alert mode to (1) when you attach it so as to enable audible feature.

Heiken ashi will sound a few times when the direction is swinging so dont go hunting for a way to turn it off, as it will do so once the directional change is confirmed and a new sound is made.  At this time a window will appear showing details of the alert an price levels applicable, simply press OK and all shall be fine.

Moving average crossover alert can be altered to whatever values you wish.   With regard to FastMA Mode the following numbers are equivalent to these settings -  0=sma, 1=ema, 2=smma, 3=lwma and 4=lsma.

Fast price mode and slow price mode can also be adjusted if you prefer close analysis of price over open etc.  The allocation for those settings are - 0=close (I have set as default) 1=open, 2=high, 3=low, 4=median, 5=typical and 6=weighted.

Anyway, hope these are of some help.

All the best.

FxN

--- 帖子 #748 ---
Hello

As promised find attached the Moving average  crossover and Heiken Ashi.

Heiken Ashi LC (Light color) is the one to use if  you wish to paste the

stochastics over the top.  Regarding this version of Heiken ashi, I am not thrilled with it and  actually turn

the alert off most of the time on the lower time frames as it  can be a

real pain during whipsaw markets.  To be honest, I dont use it but many find it helpful.

Furthermore along with keeping things simple, you can become addicted to 'finding that one extra indicator' until one day you look at the screen and the chart is awash with lines and all sorts of confusion.   Minimize and your decision actually becomes easier.  Hell, whats the worst that can happen?  Trade goes against you and thats what stops are for.

Additionally, I have added another indicator (EJ Signal with  alert) that I find

better than the MA crossover because it allows you stay in  the trade

longer without be whipped in and out by price spikes.  It works by  a

mathematical calculation over a range of bars +/- the risk figure.   I

have set the risk at 4 which is a pretty good setting but feel free  to

play around with it on different time frames.  You will note that 4  on

the M15 and H1 allows magnificent capture of pips if you use  this

indicator purely as exit tool.  For this reason the alert is a relief  in

order to walk away from trade and not be glued constantly to screen.  The  'Bars' input which is set to 1000 is merely the number of bars/candles you wish  to analyze with the indicator looking back at history.  If you wish to scroll  back further to see how the indicator performed, just increase the Bar  number.

Hope these help you out.

FxN

--- 帖子 #749 ---
Rialto

Dont fret the change to the stochastic values.  The %K and slowing values all remained the same and the only thing changed was reducing %D on all of them to 1.  This 'erases' the dotted %D line from the indicator window because it is now sitting under %K.  You have to remember that %D is the moving average of %K and this is similar to if you were to place a 1EMA on price.....you would barely see the line.

Boxingislife mentioned he reduced it to 1 for the same reason as my previous post, that being of cutting back on screen clutter, plus he uses %K merely as a measure of trend so he can glance what is happening with the slope.  Many of the other Traders on this thread decided to keep it and thats ok too.

In all the time using stochastics I have done the opposite, actually using %D as what I term a 'dynamic trend line'.  Neither method is 'wrong', its just what you find of greater efficiency.  The values I use for stochastics are totally different from Boxingislife and I merely assign %K the color black so it is invisible in indicator pane.

At the end of the day, take a breath, don't get stuck on one set of numbers thinking that they are the regimented rule that cant be broken because it has as much to do with the methodology also.  Look at adding your own 'flavor' to the system and question everything otherwise you will be following others forever.

FxN

--- 帖子 #755 ---
I spent a little bit of time modifying an indicator from scorpion over at the fxfisherman forum (thank you again scorpion!) so it will work with this system.  The indicator will check the 5, 20, and 50 stochastics to see if they are above their signal lines.  Once the 5 pulls back and crosses it will draw an arrow in the trade direction.  If only the 20 and 50 stochastics are crossed, a white arrow is drawn.  If the 20, 50, and 100 stochastics are crossed it will draw a red arrow.  Ofcourse, this indicator will only draw the arrows, the user still has to make sure the stochastics have the proper slope.

Something I have noticed after reading TEB63's thread (VERY good thread) is that when the 4 hour 5,3,3 stochastic and only the 5,3,3 stochastic is in agreement with a signal we get on the 1 hour (TEB uses daily, 4H, 30 min) it has a higher probability of working, and usually will be a bigger move.

--- 帖子 #775 ---
ok so in this example ill use eurusd 1h and a 4h chart

ill be showing you a nice pattern i guess i could call it and it will help u get better and more precise entries and will let u know when the trend should be continuing

ok as u see in the euro 4h chart all 3 stochs are above 80 and well 2 of em the 20 is starting to move down. basically we got a slingshot on the 4h. when we have a slingy we go to the 1h and notice that the 20 and 50 pull down and the 100 does too but most the time stays above 80. they form sort of like an arrow shape. so now that we know that trend is up and we got a signal on the 4h we wanna enter more precisely using the 1h chart. before we switch to the 1h we wanna wait till price consolidates on the 4h or the 5 gets to oversold territory(yellow rectangle). when that happens we go to the 1h and by then the 20 and 50 on the 1h will have started to flatten or started trending back up. when that does we wait for the signal from the 5 and enter(black triangles)

basically when we have a slingy on the 4h and the 5 pulls back all it is its the trend taking a break on the 1h so that way we can wait for the break to be over and enter rather than just using the 4h to enter and using big stops. this way we can enter using the 1h and with smaller stops and a better entry and we know that action should be happening soon.

in more simple terms:

4h chart

1: slingy

2: price consolidates or the 5 gets to oversold/overbought

1h chart

1: all 3 stochs pull back a bit

2: watch for flattening stochs or for em to start movin back with the trend

3: we enter on the first signal using the 5

remember
A SLINGY ON THE 4H IS NOTHING BUT A SMALL PAUSE IN THE TREND ON THE 1H

thats really the main thing to look for and im showing u a way to recognize it and enter more precisely

obviously the more confirmation u got the better like the more stochs u got above 80 or below 20 the better.

sorry if this seems confusing but check the example and post some examples and ill tell u if its right. all it is its a way to recognize when the trend is continuing and enter accordingly. all using 2 timeframes. of course itl work with daily and 4h or any 2 combos. or at least it should work but with 4h and 1h its what i mostly focus on if i have time.

edit: with some practice u guys will love it and itl help u make some serious cash. trend following=$$$$

itl take u guys some time to grasp it but trust me its worth it. itl also save u from taking trades on the 1h that are against the trend of the 4h which could be killer.

--- 帖子 #796 ---
Hitch.

Once you have one window open with a Stocs indicator, click the Navigator button. This opens up a pane on the left hand side that lists Accounts, Indicators, Experts, etc. In the Indicators list, find Stochastics indicator and click and drag in onto the Stocs window that is already open. A parameters box will open. Make sure you give this Stocs different parameters from the first or it won't show up. Click and drag as many Stocs indicators as you want into this window.

--- 帖子 #812 ---
profit taking can really depend on alot. first of all check a few pages back i think i explained how i deal with profit taking

the easiest way to do this is get out when the 5 gets to oversold or overbought. thats very simple and straightforward.

as u gain experience ull start to know more about the pair u trade and how much it moves and how much can u aim for and things like that

it also depends on the timeframe. u cant aim for 50 pips using a signal from the 5 min chart. u might get lucky and it would be a nice move from just one signal but chances are it would either take a break every little bit and scare u or it just wont reach more than 10 or 15 pips.

basically aim depending on the timeframe ur using

but for starters i suggest u get out when the 5 gets to oversold or overbought its as simple as that and u should make really good money.

take care

my absolute favorite is the 4h because its not too long term but its not too fast either it works great for a guy like me that spends most of his day at university

also the 1h is great

basically pick a timeframe that fits ur schedule. then pick one pair or 2 or a few if u can watch em all and just trade the best setups. do some visual backtesting and learn about each pairs daily range and the way it works and place ur stops accordingly. get out when the 5 gets to oversold or overbought and  I GUARANTEE you that you will come out profitable every month and not less than 8-9 profitable trades out of 10

not sounding like im psychic or anything but when usdcad was at 1.17-18 and i said we got a great signal on the monthly and i was aiming for 1.10 or even 1.05.... well i wasnt kidding  lol and it just goes to show that even a very boring and long term signal on the monthly can kick some serious ass

imagine if u were trading just lots of 1k not even mini lots. taking every 4h and daily signal you get and basically adding on pullbacks since you know the trend is down according to the monthly chart. just imagine what kind of money you could have banked. im gonna be honest i stopped trading usdcad but i did bank about 200 or so pips trading multi lots .

edit : more detailed explanation

1st blue box

1 : first color change of NLMA (down), not valid, there is no 5 cross and 20 are uptrend

2 : 2nd color change of NLMA (up ) valid, 5 cross in oversold (OS) and 20 uptrend

2nd blue box

NLMA color change down (at the right of the box), valid but not very rewarding but not loosing

3rd blue box

I dont even see how you can see a signal ??? The onyl valid signal is the next NLMA color change out of the box on the right side

edit2 : also, MA cross is for EXIT only !!! Not for entry, please read the guide more carefully. The entry point is determined byt the stoch 5/20/50 in combination and by the NLMA filter only...

--- 帖子 #868 ---
So guys, it seems like many of you would like to have a chat room on this method, but I saw only few people in #sexy IRC channel. And I decided to make some kind of guide on how to use IRC and join the chat. Btw we've changed channels name to #stoch_traders_group to avoid those sexy lovers =).

1. The simpliest way is to go to ircatwork.com as Melpheous mentioned.

Nickname: type in your nick.

Server:irc.opera.com

Channel:#stoch_traders_group

Thats it.

2. You can also download software-based chat platform (I use xChat/xchat.org or you may use mIRC/mirc.com or even Opera/opera.com).

When you run xChat first time you will see a dialog window "Network list". You should enter your nickname, user name etc. Then press +Add button, type "Opera" in new row appeared. Press "Edit" and in a new dialog window  ("Edit Opera") you should press "Edit" again and type in irc.opera.com in "Server for Opera" field. Almost done. The last step is when you type #stoch_traders_group in "Channels to join". Thats it. Now you can join the chat by pressing "Connect".

Just my 2 cents..................

--- 帖子 #883 ---
tzachi

each time frame has different stops

u cant use a 15-20 pip stop on a 1h gbpusd trade

but u should easily be able to on a 15 min trade

just because the 1h isnt showing a signal doesnt mean the 15 min is a bad signal. basically look at it this way, the more confirmation u have the better

so if u have a trade on the 15 min chart to go long and the 1h is pointing up or the price has been moving up nicely then it would be a good signal

if u see the 1h pointing down and the 15 min just gave u a signal to buy then it would obviously be a bad trade or one u should avoid. **edited

u dont need the 1h to look exactly the same as a 15 min chart to take the trade but at least make sure its not the opposite. does that make sense?

dont confuse urself with timeframes and confirmations. if ur worried just start with 1 timeframe and only take the best trades. alot of trades i have taken i never bothered to look at a different timeframe because the setup was just so good. if it fails it fails and it can happen all the time

--- 帖子 #890 ---
I played a little bit today and created this little indicator that show all situation in a single view about the buy/sell signal that this method is giving on different Stoch for multiple timeframe from M5 to H1.

Stoch5 means Stochastic(5,3,3), Stoch20 means Stochastic(20,10,20) and Stoch50 means Stochastic(50,10,20).

If arrow is pointing up (green) then is a buy signal otherwise if it's pointing down (red) is a sell. The more arrow of the same direction/color we get the more the signal is stronger.

Anyway discretional is still to be used , since the trader should check for the single timeframe to see where the various stoch are.

http://img78.imageshack.us/img78/614/gbpusdm5rn8.jpg

In attachment you can find also sexy stochastic template shown in the above picture.

Hope it could be helpfull

Cheers,

Hi melpheos,

We all know about the limitations with backtesting but these results are nothing but sensational if they are close to what would have happened.

For your second test you state that these were at better risk as you used the 90/10 levels but if your fist test is valid I don't think that a 98% win rate can be sniffed at. This is actually higher than the second safer test, which achieved 97%.

The trade rate is also interesting.

Test 1 : 204 trades in 621 calender days, which equates to appx 1 trade every 2.25 trading days.

Test 2 : 35 trades in 716 calender days, which equates to appx 1 trade every 14.5 trading days.

From this I would think that the 'safer' method doesn't offer any real advantage.

--- 帖子 #954 ---
Hi guys,

i would like to share a thing with you all because i think that will help you all to archive more profit with your current system.I work at a bank right now as trader and the first thing i learned at my day 1 is: Its IMPOSSIBLE to blow a account with a bad trading system, but its easy to blow up a entire account with a good trading system.

Ill explain here : When you get a trigger with any system you are using right now, you expect the price to move in one direction, North or South. The first thing you need to determine is, how many pips this trigger can possibly make, for exemple ill say 50 pips in North direction. ok now we have the first information to analise what we will do. The second thing is to find a corfirmation to be sure our trigger was a good one and not a wispaw. For that you need to think how many pips you will let in the market for your safety trigger. in this exemple ill say 15 pip.

Now we have all our information needed to take a trade,ill place a pending order 15 pip upper than the current price(Pending order), if my trigger is hit , good , if not well , was a wispaw.Dont wait 2 hour before removing your pending order if it didnt get reach.MOnitor permanently your position , you dont know if you will archive your 35 pip (50 - 15).Always trade with 2 lot. half way close 50% of your position and put BreakEven + 1 for your last 50%, its your runner, maybe you was wrong and the price will retrace and hit your BE+1 ,no big deal, im at leat + 1 pips up on this one but maybe the trend will continue like hell and ill make 200 pips, nobody know and even bank.

Using that, if you get a crappy day with a bunch of wispaw, you will maybe loose some pips but 80% will be avoided.The only and the most important thing is you need to understand your current trading system to know how it react with the market. if usualy each trigger can make 30 pip, use about 1/4 for your safety so in this exemple 7-8 pips, but its up to you , each trading system use different parameter so find yours.

Market order is used to trade News, USA are good, Sell eur/usd , USA are bad, Buy eur/usd. Pending order are for safe trade when you dont know exactly where the market go.

The last thing is "Why the market move in this direction and not in this way", Often you will see the market going crazy and its not cuz people are trading to make money.If a bank need 400million Euro cuz a custumer request that, the bank will buy 400million euro and sell X USD, that will move the market for no reason. Alot of people use Visa, and you can Buy about anything in different currency using you Visa card , Visa need to convert some big amount of money too , and trow the order to bank who will buy/sell.Its why you can get alot of wispaw as a Technical trader. So you need a safety,and your safety trigger is by not buying the current market price.

I hope that information can help some of you

Best Regards,

EricFX

P.S Sorry for my bad english

--- 帖子 #957 ---
Hi all,

New to this thread, but have been trading with Boxing for many months.

I am having the same problems with the EA, I can't run an EX4 file with my broker.

Here is an excellent thread on backtesting, which highlights some of the pitfalls, and the correct way to go about it and how to optimise settings without "over-optimising" by applying the 75/25 rule. http://www.strategybuilderfx.com/sho...ight=illusions

Basically this is how it works..... optimising a reasonable system will give amazing results...by definition we are optimising the best possible results based on the past data. That is not necessarily a great indicator of future results.

The 75/25 rule means that if you take 2 years historical 1 min data and use the first 18 months for optimising, then the following 6 months to validate the optimised results, to see what validity there was. Following this, a further live demo forward test should be run for a few weeks to ensure it works, then it can be run on a live account.

The backtesting without a stop doesnt demonstrate anything, as noticed by many of you. By following the above methodology to ascertain the appropriate stop and tp for each timeframe and pair will greatly assist.

Here is another strategy using Heiken Ashi methods, including using it for an exit strategy. http://www.compassfx.com/comp/Dean_M...ing_Method.pdf

His exit for a long (page 57 of this document) is based on:

1. The positive bar is much shorter than the previous bar, or

2. Changes to a negative bar at close.

I'd be very interested to get any feedback on using this as the exit point.

I hope this helps.

Matt

--- 帖子 #962 ---
This is because of the new MT4 version (standard) which shows a 5th decimal. If you look the orders, the figures are weird when the order close for a loss (like missing a decimal here and there)

ATM, the EA is not able to close any trade but because of a TP reached or because of a forced close because of margin call.

This is why i think this EA with it's near 100% rate could be a real winner but without the implementation of a SL it is not possible to do proper backtests (for example, the first trade in the latest backtest goes around minus 40-50 before turning back and reaching the TP so if you had a SL of 30, the trade would not have been profitable, this was checked with visual testing )

if the safer offer the same success rate with a far bigger pipcount we also need to do a ratio.

method1 : 1 trade every 2 day with a 10 pips return would give in 1000 days 5000 pips

method2 : 1 trade every 10 days with 70 pips return would give in 1000 days 7000 pips

It is just a stupid example but you see my point

Hey all,

I have been studying this method for 3 weeks now and have been trading it live for the last 2 weeks. I am trading GBP/JPY, GBP/USD, EUR/USD, & USD/JPY. The first week was good at +220 pips. This week was my best week at +365 pips. I am doing this part time, by being able to be in front of my computer roughly 15 hours per week. I use Interbank FX for charts and Oanda for my trades.

I simplified this system this week as follows .... I mainly look at 1hour charts. When the Blue 20,10,20 stoch line changes slope/direction and comes up from below 30 I am ready to buy long. I then wait for the 5,3,3 stoch to reload (best if it goes below 20 and heads up, but mainly just changes direction). Then I place my trade. (The same holds true only reverse for shorts....Blue 20,10,20 stoch line goes down from 70)

I am getting out one of three ways..... when the 5,3,3 stoch hits the 80 line or reverses or I get chicken and want to book pips (usually 15 to 35 pips then close trades). Not being greedy is OK. I started the week trading 3000 units and built confidence. Toward the end of the week some trades were 10,000 units. Obviously, nothing to get rich with, but fits my style, and want to book consistent pips before increasing $.

Stop loss at 50 to 75.

I started Sunday and made 17 trades thru today. 15 trades closed positive for +390 pips, 2 trades I closed out for -19 pips and -6 pips (the 5,3,3 stoch was losing steam and got scared). None hit my stop loss.

This simple system, part time netted me $213 for this week.

Best advise I can give is there are tons of 15 - 35 pip reversals/trends during each week that are identified by this system. Don't look at other systems. Don't be greedy. Catch as many reversals/trends as time allows you. Gain confidence in your version of this system. Book pips and do it over the long term. Keep it simple.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #983 ---
I've been studying today how the MA Cross buy and sell arrows work. They aren't actually confirmed until after the full period has been completed for the candle following the one it appears on.

For example, on an hourly chart in GBP/USD, the candle for 0100 to 0200 is formed, then the following candle starts moving down, and a down arrow appears above the 0100, then there is a sharp spike up at 0225, and the direction of the arrow may then REVERSE to going up. The only time that it  can be assumed that the arrow direction is likely to be correct is when the following candle has been completed. In this example it is going to be at 0300.

When you look at it on the charts however, you see this amazing trade as though the signal could have got you in at the start of the first candle, not at the end of the second one. On a 1 hour candle this can make the difference of 100-200 pips in GBP/USD.

--- 帖子 #984 ---
As said before, the MA crossover signal is for exit only not for entry... Also, it is my exit strategy and unfortunately there is no perfect exit strategy

--- 帖子 #985 ---
Thanks for clarifying Melpheos. I just wanted to make sure that anyone else that was looking at the charts like i have been was aware of this fact.

Have a look at the following as potential exit signals (for short trades)....I have been studying GBP/USD 1 hour charts, so they are "fitted" for that pair and timeframe, but my aim was to ensure that the trade stayed in till the bottom, but exited at about the correct time:

1. Stoch 5,4,3. The 4 line turns up higher than the end of the previous period.

2. Stoch 10,8,3. The 8 crosses the 10. This appears a much better exit signal than the 5,3,3 with the 3 crossing the 5, as you stay in longer for the longer moves rather than getting shaken out.

Only exit for each at the end of the bar, if the condition still holds.

I'd be interested to hear your thoughts. Please note that I am still experimenting with these settings, after developing them through observation.

Cheers,

Matt.

--- 帖子 #991 ---
Melph. I hate to be rude mate. But the only filter needed on an indicator based system, is knowledge. You cannot filter an indicator with an indicator. Even if its "nonlag" aka "repainting".

Having used this system now for 3 days on the 15 minute time frame, I have made 190 pips. Only 1 loss and it was very small. But its as the author said, its all about taking the best set up.

There is no point turning it into an EA or adding extra indicators. It just clutters your screen and makes things pointless. An EA will always promote loss. We all know that.

Best bet is to start from the beginning again, and enjoy the profits.

--- 帖子 #992 ---
i'm no pointing an EA... The point of the nonlagma filter is to take more successfull trade than with the original method.

I agree with the fact that if you wait for the perfect setup you should have around 95% success rate (i have tested it this way myself) but i can't be in front of my PC all the time this is the reason why i worked for a filter that could allow you to take more trade.

The reason of this filter is because i take what boxingislife call halfbroke trade ^^ and taking those require a filter.

Also, the stochastic are not a filter but an indicator used as a signal and in the default setup the 50 act as a filter.

If you remove the 50, you need a different filter hence the use of nonlagma.

Ps: no worries, you are not rude. You are just posting your point of view

The green are the 5, the bold red/blue are the 20, the ticked line are the 50...

You can see which indicator is which by hovering the line with you mouse. Please try to make some effort and read, read, read...

--- 帖子 #1100 ---
I have been working on a version of this system for EUR/CHF 15 minute chart. Please find attached my template which is fairly basic, the stoch 5,3,3 and Stoch 20, 10, 20, along with a bollinger 2, 20 period and a bollinger 3, 20 period.

Basically use the stochs as confirmation with the bollinger band level 2 when EURCHF is trading nicely in a band. Look for small profits around 9 pips per trade with relatively wide stops, around 17 or so....scalping heaven.  Other versions of this system that I have been trialling have had 86% win rates in backtesting with 9 pip tp and 17 pip stop.

I would only trade this when the Bollinger band level 2 high band and low band are around 18 pips apart, and avoid trading close to news time for either EUR or CHF, as well as major news in USD. If there is a slight trend, only trade in the direction of the trend.

--- 帖子 #1108 ---
After many long coding nights, it's here! The SexyBack Indicator!! This takes into account all of the 'perfect' indicator triggers in Melphoes PDF Guide.

Instructions:Download both files and place them into your indicators directory.  Load MT4.  Pick your favorite pair and timeframe. load whatever other indicators you want. load this one. It will place text in the lower right corner of the chart window telling you if it's a 'buy', 'sell', or 'calm down sparky' (flat) indicator.

Settings:Global_Corner: what corner of the chart window you want the indicator to appear. Integer. 0=Upper Left, 1=Upper Right, 2=lower left , 3=lower right Xdist and Ydist: The distance from absolute 0 (0,0) on the XY cordinates. Not sure how it's actually measured, but I found 3 for each to be good. StochLevelDown: The bottom Stoch level you want the 5 main to go below. Read PDF for further explanation StochLevelUp: The top Stoch level you want the 5 main to be above. Read PDF for further explanation Beta test and let me know what you guys think. Post all requests, problems, etc. here. I'll get to them when I can.

THANKS!
-Nondiscloseure00 (It's actually supposed to be Nondisclosure007, but FF took off the last character.  ).

PS. Thanks to igorad for the new NonLagMA indicator. You can find the post of it here.

Ok gang, here's the latest.  It's getting there.  I could really use some help on figuring out the Stoch's and what they should be.

Here's the 'pseduo' code:

If Stoch(20,10,20) > Stoch(50,10,20) and

Stoch(20,10,20) > It's signal line; and

Stoch(50,10,20) > It's signal line; and

NonLagMA trend is going up; and

Stoch(5,3,3) > It's signal line; then

BUY!

If Stoch(20,10,20) < Stoch(50,10,20) and

Stoch(20,10,20) < It's signal line; and

Stoch(50,10,20) < It's signal line; and

NonLagMA trend is going down; and

Stoch(5,3,3) < It's signal line; then

SELL!

Anything else and we leave it alone.
