--- 帖子 #1141 ---
If think the way it is handle is not good.

The stoch 5,3,3 have to be handle by a cross and not by a direction.

you have to stay with

If Stoch(20,10,20) > Stoch(50,10,20) and

Stoch(20,10,20) > It's signal line; and

Stoch(50,10,20) > It's signal line and

stoch 20,10,20 is going up

stoch 50,10,20 is going up

Stoch 5,3,3 has cross below a certain level (that you can define with a extern int ) with the stoch 5,3,3 going up and the stoch 5,3,3 still going up

the nonlagma is going up after a maximum of a certain numbre of bar (that you can define as well but i have seen up to 4 bar for a good setup)

But you need to make sure that if the stoch 5,3,3 cross to the downward, a code would say to stop considering the nonlagma.

I believe it would be something like

if stoch 5,3,3 cross upward then X=1

if stoch 5,3,3 cross downard then X=2

You are right, need to wait one more hour for the setup to be confimed (on my plateform it's gmt+2)

--- 帖子 #1161 ---
This is the rules i think should be Ok to program for an EA.

I'll explain for buy only as sell is only the buy signal reversed

So here we go

Stoch 5 :

- current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch)

- candle -1 is lower than candle -2 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch )

- candle -1 is lower than set level (for example 60)

Stoch 20 : current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level (for example 2, this is to prevent a very light slope of the stoch)

Stoch 20 : current candle K% is higher than current candle D% by at least a defined level

(for example 5, this is to simulate distance between the stoch and it's signal line)

Stoch 50 : current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level

(for example 5, this is to prevent a very low slope of the stoch)

Stoch 50 : current candle K% is higher than current candle D% by at least a defined level

(for example 5, this is to simulate distance between the stoch and it's signal line)

NonlagMA V5 : current candle is higher than candle -1 (no need to define the level but being able to define the different parameters of the Nonlagma would be great for backtesting )

Note that NonlagmaV5 often turns after the stoch5 have reversed, for this reason here is an added set of rules for this situation (i have tried to make them but the code became very messy and i got lost )

Stoch 5 :

Stoch 5 :

- current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch)

- candle -1 is lower than candle -2 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch )

- candle -2 is lower than candle -3 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch )

- candle -2 is lower than set level (for example 60)

Stoch 20 : current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level (for example 2, this is to prevent a very light slope of the stoch)

Stoch 20 : current candle K% is higher than current candle D% by at least a defined level

(for example 2, this is to simulate distance between the stoch and it's signal line)

Stoch 50 : current candle is higher than candle -1 by at least a defined level

(for example 2, this is to prevent a very low slope of the stoch)

Stoch 50 : current candle K% is higher than current candle D% by at least a defined level

(for example 5, this is to simulate distance between the stoch and it's signal line)

NonlagMA V5 : current candle is higher than candle -1 (no need to define the level but being able to define the different parameters of the Nonlagma would be great for backtesting )

This process should be done for at least 3-4 candles (usually after 4 candles the signal is not good enough or the setup is not here anymore like the 5 in oversold )

But there is for sure a smarter way to make a good code.

Additional note after looking the level on good setup on my chart : the defined level should adjustable of course

forgot one detail but i think that was obvious (to me ^^ )

current candle refers to closed candle and of course each candle rule refers to it's signal.

So for example :

Stoch 5 :

- current closed candle stoch 5is higher than candle -1 stoch 5 by at least a defined level (for example 5 to prevent a light slope of the stoch)

I think the code in this case is

extern bool EachTickMode = False

int init() {

BarCount = Bars;

if (EachTickMode) Current = 0; else Current = 1;

return(0);

}

I am a definite newbie to Forex, I have been reviewing this system  and would like to suggest adding another Stochastic under this one with the settings of %K 140, %D 4, slowing to 1.  Under the Levels tab add a 50 line. When the lines cross the 50 line, either going up or down then time to consider, I have been using just this indicator with good success. The lower the time frame (TF) the more pips it can yield because of the earlier entry but higher risk. Please back test this and you will see good entry points, and some not so good. On good 1 or 2 day moves the exit becomes the 50 line again. The indicator will pin itself either to the top or the bottom indicating the trend is strong. Been tested that a 30 pip trailing stop can be close to the same as the 50 line exit. The tricky part is always the entry. I can see using these two together might swing the probability a little more our way. If anyone wants pictures I can post some if the understanding needs to be clarified. I believe this system can swing the probability towards the positive side even more. Any thoughts would be appreciated.

--- 帖子 #1331 ---
3 helpful hints when trading live:

1.  ALWAYS use a stoploss.  set it for what your risk tolerance is.

2.  Use a Trailing Stop.  This will help you lock in profits just in case you miss when the market goes against your trade.

3.  Never risk more that 20% available equity, not balance.  Some brokers will only give you half of your balance as available equity.  Don't know why, but some do.  I had one like that and I dropped them fast.

--- 帖子 #1332 ---
I have been looking at the 4hr strategy by Phillip Nel at http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=14630 and I suggest it is a good system for exit to combine with sexy.

I noted earlier folk were discussing the idea of finding a good exit strategy, and looking at Phillip's system has some advantages on the exit, as in many cases, it signals to keep in the trade to collect those extra pips before the reversal.

Sexy tends to give an earlier entry signal, and his system tends to give a later exit signal. A comparison backtest would be in order to see if my hunch is correct, but merely from a cursory perusal of the charts lends me to this conclusion.

Any other comments on this?

Frank

--- 帖子 #1342 ---
Maybe the order of k D and slowing are different in VT...

My K is 3 and my slowing is 3... It looks on your chart that your slowing is 1 rather than 3...

For the 20/50 it looks more or less the same, also remember that our data provider are different so different chart (but with 4H it should be quite similar)

Play with the fast stoch settings and uses the one you feel at ease.

I generaly dont look at the crossing of the fast stoch but it can gives false signal if you follow the system blindly so i would suggest you keep the D% at 3 or 5

ur right

the 5 3 3 doesnt have to pull back all the way to oversold overbought the most important part is the cross with its signal line and to head in the direction of the slow moving stochastics

best time frames is really all about experiencing

if i see a really good signal on the 4h then thats my priority

if no good signals or choppy market then i look at the general trend

and i go down to the 1h and the 15 min

when the 1h gives me a signal then i go to the 15 min to catch a better entry and some of the tiny retracements that happen during the move which brings u the most pips if u practice a bit

exits when the 5 gets to oversold or overbought is the easiest and probably the best way to exit

i got other ways of exiting that are more accurate but thats somethin i cant share. my own personal work

mac doug

i see ur usin it-finance

i had access to their charts through prorealtime and i had access to ticks.

a suggestion for you since not alot of people use ticks with forex(more with futures and stocks) set up a 150 tick chart then a 450 tick chart then a 1000 tick chart. ticks are alot better since they arent time based so it sort of filters the dead hours. if u have access to the tick charts, give it a shot and ull see how nice price trends on ticks and how easy it is o pick up pips. back in the summer on volatile days i was picking up 200-300 pips a day with gbpjpy using tick charts.

I spent alot of time with spud and tebs mtf stochastic threads. I actually find this technique much simpler and clearer cause its all on one chart. I use other general tech analysis techniques such as trendlines and pivot points to filter trades and determine entries and exits. This signal avoids the confusion that can occur using mtf when different time frames conflict. I love it!

Melpeos, I notice there are no %d lines in your stochs. How are u determining wether %k has crossed %d or are you just using slope of %k lines or a cross of the 20 and 50 to determine direction?

--- 帖子 #1410 ---
In fact there is no k% line

What you can see is the %d line using smooth and period 2.

As i use really fast %k period (4) i had to filter the whipsaw those using the %d line smoothed.

Put the following settings 4-2-2 and look when a cross occurs.

You will see that each time a cross occurs (around 95% of the time) it occurs on the next candle where the stoch makes a reversal. As normally you look for a cross of k and d and take the trade, using only reversal of the stoch allow me to take the trade usually one candle before the cross.

I'll probably make a new edition of my guide to explain this.

In fact i'm working now on something new i have just discovered this morning. This have to do with stochs but is fairly different from Boxingislife system.

edit : woops wrong reading, but yes i use mainly the slope, completed with the price action, it's more than enough to determine the trend.

edit2 : apparently, boxing is also using only one line yet he still uses %k and not %d...

I would think that trading on the shorter tf, like you do, melphos, would return the similar number of pips as trading on the longer tf. Maybe, go in with lower lots on the longer tf, since the pips gain would be larger, but you can keep your losses at the same amt as if you were trading on the shorter tf.

But most of the time there are a few trades in the day. All trades are on 15M tf, and only two types, rubber band (snap back of shorter tf stoch), and go with intra-day trend (longer tf stoch coming out of 80/20, wait for smaller tf stoch to retrace, and then come back in line with longer tf stochs). I just have not been able to see a loss. Now I know that in trading, there are always losses. I am patient, only looking for a trade that meets my criteria 100%, nothing that is like a "lets see what the market does"!!!

--- 帖子 #1442 ---
Hi kermut

Welcome aboard the sexy stoch gravy train. I hope to see many more posts from you

I agree, its a real problem not having bad signals- I have lost one trade so far but I just spent half an hour looking for it or any  signal failure and the only ones I could find werent good signals in the first place! With the right set of rules, observance of support and resistance and market times, it is very difficult to lose a trade. Melpheos has been doing it alot longer than me  so perhaps he will be able to find you a bad signal. They do occur.

The theory behind its effectiveness is simple. It waits for a trend to develop, and then waits for a retracement of that trend. It then waits for confirmation that the retracement has exhausted before signaling an entry. Lots of waiting and patience is built in. All the hard work is done by the indicator. Brilliant!

In short, it sells rallies in a downtrend and buys dips in an uptrend. That is a successful formula but is difficult to do with a  discretionary technique.

I also use pivots to filter entries and to determine conservative targets and stop loss levels and I have a few other rules regarding the stoch set up. I take notice of candlestick reversal patterns also. I usually trade one hour or higher though. I would love to talk more about this with you as it seems our techniques are similar. Perhaps we may be able to contribute something new to the already great work of melpheos, boxingislife and others

meanwhile here is a signal that entered just prior to market consolidation at about midday New York Time. It still would have been difficult to lose or at least break even because it did manage to get 50 pips in front before reversing but thats the best 'failure' I could find so far

(oops, melpheos replied while i was doing my reply so some of this post is now obsolete)

--- 帖子 #1455 ---
To put these 3 stochs together u can just , open list with indicators on ur left side  and "drag and drop" every stoch on same place.

It means , u can "drag and drop" 5,3,3 to main chart , and next "drag and drop" 20 stoch on previous 5,3,3 and it will set them together in 1 place , and same make with 50 stoch .

and u will have 3 stochs in 1 window.

if u will read whole thread ull see that this topic was before

--- 帖子 #1500 ---
Dear Prosperfx,

I have read through the thread twice and have been sporadically demo trading the method. I believe it has merit. How much merit will depend on the trader's consistency, etc.---things we all know about. Boxing stochastics is simply a retracement system which uses short-term momentum within the context of longer-term momentum as its core indicator. Which I find interesting. And it gets more interesting, I believe, if you jibe two timeframes, as Moonchild has suggested in the past. But as with all discretionary systems, there are nuances to the indicator "look" which transcend the simple rules and hence require a good deal of self-training to get right. The question really becomes, does one have the persistence to look and look and look some more until not just the main rules are clear in your head but that the nuance issues have also been ironed out---which is, in the end, the only way to make the model your own.

Lenoxer

--- 帖子 #1501 ---
I think you described better than i could have the "issue" with this system.

If you follow blindly the signal you will have a very poor success rate ratio because you also have to look what the price is doing before taking a trade.

You can get a signal when there was a 68% pull back and a pull back in this pull back. In this kind of situation, there is big chance that the signal you got at the first place is invalidate and you are more in a reversal pattern.

Finaly, whatever strategy you use, it's all about price action...

The more i trade, the more i can read the chart without looking at the indicators.

--- 帖子 #1516 ---
Dear Boxing Thread,

What I have been observing anecdotally, ala Moonchild's jibing of timeframes,

is that if one waits for an unfinished signal on the 60" (20 and 50 stochs properly paralleled and sloped with the 5-3-3 left uncrossed) and then segues to any one of the 1"-5" charts and waits for a perfect signal---on whichever micro timeframe the signal occurs first---that the market noise of the 60" chart is then neutralized without sacrificing too much to lag and all while preserving the pip range possibilities of the upper timeframe. Additionally, to then use the scattershot approach of Aleksey's hybrids (search on FF for Aleksey) for money management seems sound. How, though, to determine the best MAE stops for these trades? Your thoughts?

Thanks,

Lenoxer

--- 帖子 #1517 ---

--- 帖子 #1533 ---
Dear Jont,

Do a search for Aleksey and then for FXTradePro on FF. Read the first few pages of each thread to get the idea. Aleksey trades what he calls hybrids, four pairs of completely unrelated currencies. His idea is that this is the best diversification of all. FXTradePro uses a martingale EA which, crudely put, doubles up on losing, stop-and-reverse trades until a profit is achieved. To apply FXTradePro's EA on Aleksey's hybrids strikes me as a way of knocking down human error, otherwise known as trader risk. Additionally, I've asked my traders to read the following link: http://www.newyorker.com/reporting/2..._fact_gawande/

This is an article about the use of checklists. The success statistics quoted in the article are impressive. Why can't a good checklist be made and used for traders as well?

Hope this helps. Look forward to yours and others' responses.

Lenoxer

--- 帖子 #1535 ---
I think martingale is for people who cant handle taking a loss. The problem with it is you cannot guarantee a losing streak of 10 or more consequtive trades will not occur. by that time your account is gone. You have to start with such a small risk to allow for a losing streak that the reward becomes not worth while and each trade is actually risking your entire account balance on a bet that that you wont have a run of losers. One day you will lose that bet.

as for aleksey, check my post no 39 on his thread for where I am currently at with that guy

--- 帖子 #1539 ---
Dear Maacavity,

The simple answer is: don't trade if there is conflict between timeframes. The beautiful thing about Forex is that if this trade doesn't look good, there will be another one soon that will. As boxing once pointed out (and where is that guy, anyway?), why take less than perfect trades? The more complicated answer is: take the setup if it looks good enough (beautifully sloping longer term stochs with a good deep retracement on the 5-3-3), and be cognizant of the upper TFs to the degree that you need to be nimble with your risk control. Good luck.

Lenoxer

--- 帖子 #1544 ---
Hi Maccavity

I find that if all the time frames line up (rare), that there will be a very strong move in one direction for an intense period of time, with very little retracement.  However, that is rare.

In another Stochs Forum, a guy called Spud (where is he now?) would emphasize:  the lower time frames build the larger.

I personally start on the lower time frames (I try to always enter on the 1 min, and exit) and work up to the larger, occasionally they will all line up, but that is not a normal trading day.  If the 15min TF shows the 5 stoch in good sling shot position (retraced), but the 5 minute chart is heading down, the 15 minute will wait until the 5 does a "complete round" before it moves in the way you hope it to.

I like to think of small to big, rather than the other way around.

Using the lower time frame charts you learn to read (I'm very much still learning) and predict what is going to happen in the larger time frames.

I will try and find some pictures to illustrate.

--- 帖子 #1548 ---
First using smooth remove some whipsaw.

Secondly, as i use 4.2.2 i have to remove whipsaw

3rd, using 4.2.2 with smooth give me the possibility to look only the V and /\ pattern for the fast stoch.

Using the signal line instead of the main line gives an easier view of the setup (you have only 3 lines instead of 6 )

And yes, sometimes (not all the time) looking for V and /\ instead of signal/main cross can give a signal one candle before the cross.

Also look closely what happens when there is a V or /\ shape. There is about 95% of the time a cross of the main and the signal line so why losing time and having a heavier chart ?

--- 帖子 #1569 ---
Squeeze is when Bollinger Bands get inside Keltner Channel - in short

What values for both you should use, hmm dont know you should experiment

here is explanation in more details

from

http://transcripts.fxstreet.com/2006...ing_volat.html

For students of Bollinger Bands, periods of low volatility are identified as the times when the bands “move closer together.” This is always great in hindsight, but in real time, how does a trader know that the current narrowness is really narrow enough to qualify as low volatility? This setup answers that question by adding the Keltner Channels as well as a momentum index oscillator.
John Carter (Mar 9, 2006 11:49:58 AM)

For readers who are unaware of how these indicators work, I’ll take a few moments to explain them here. Bollinger Bands are a type of envelope that is plotted at standard deviation levels above and below a moving average. This produces an effect of having the bands widen during periods of higher volatility and contract during less volatile periods. During periods of lower volatility, in sideways moving markets, the bands contract toward the moving average. Keltner Channels are based on a standard moving average. The actual band lines are offset by a positive and negative standard deviation value from the central moving average value, to provide upper and lower bands. While the Bollinger Bands expand and contract as the markets alter between periods of high and low volatility, the Keltner Channels stay in more of a steady range.
John Carter (Mar 9, 2006 11:51:54 AM)

The quiet periods I’m looking for are identified when the Bollinger Bands narrow in width to the point that they are actually trading inside of the Keltner Channels. This marks a period of reduced volatility and signals that the market is taking a significant breather, building up steam for its next move. The trade signal occurs when the Bollinger Bands then move back outside the Keltner Channels

--- 帖子 #1570 ---
John Carter (Mar 9, 2006 11:52:47 AM)

I use a 12-period momentum index oscillator to determine whether to go long or short. If the oscillator is above zero when this happens, I go long; if it is below zero, I go short. These are all canned studies that come with most charting packages. For the parameters, I just use the default settings on TradeStation. These readings are 20 and1.5 for the Keltner Channels and 20 and 2 for the Bollinger Bands. I also took an extra step and turned all these into an indicator which makes it easier to read on the chart, which I explain in a moment.

------------

Now it is system for self, but if you take only squeeze without momentum to indentify buy or sell signal we could use it as indicator for consolidation period and avoid getting in on stoch signals, or at least that is my idea for now.

Well, in fact you can use the pdf as a main line but you should not focus on it as YOUR trading method.

As a fact, i'm not using the nonlag ma, nor heiken ashi anymore. The more you get used to charting, the less indicator you have on your charts. Sometime, i dont even look at the stochastics because i see a known pattern. You have to remember that stochastics are just a way to see easily what you can't see on the chart and they should not be traded blindly.

I still keep BB because they show visualy good exit point when the price go far above/below it.

Other indicator are mainly helpers and i use them because i'm used to used them.

You can see my settings on the last screenshot i have posted. The only difference with Boxingislife is the faster Fast stochastic and the fact that i follow the smoothed signal line and not the main line.

One sugestion: you could have another profile with that information but on main graph it should be as clean as possible, at least behind the price window (and you should have less zoom to have more bars on the window).

Usually I'm trading EURJPY (as it is the pair with the biggest correlation with Stock Market) on M1, M5, M15 time frame. To trade on H4, H1 you need to have wider Stop Loss which my emotions doesn't allow me to have.

Besides the indicatores Boxingislife and Melpheos suggested I added a small line to ADX values and another to daily ranges of the pair (I could have add ATR but I prefer this one). I also added two Moving Averages that could help me confirming the signals. Right now I'm testing EMA5/EMA8 and EMA9/EMA26 (reading Mechanical Trading Systems: Pairing Trader Psychology with Technical Analysis (Wiley Trading) I found the cross EMA 9 and EMA 26 has the best statistical record).

Looking for your charts, none of the time frames have Stoch-20 or Stoch-50 above 80 or below 20 so I would not take any trade.

On H4 Stoch-20 and Stoch-50 were starting to climb but stopped and are flat. On H1 Stoch-20 and Stoch-50 dropped 80 line a few bars ago so I would be inclined to go short. On M15 Stoch-20 and Stoch-50 are near oversold but Stoch-4 is also very low. I would wait to Stoch-4 to go up and when it drop I would check if Stoch-20 and Stoch-50 would be oversold and going down. If all that happens I would SELL.

But definitely I would trade another more volatile pair.

--- 帖子 #1629 ---
Hi,

As I told before, I programmed the StochV-Melpheos-ACS.mq4 for another platform and did some backtesting. The results were rather disappointing although I've missing a critical factor: Multi-TimeFrame correlation.

I tested EURJPY both on M15 and M5, from 2-Jan-2007 to 15-Feb-2008, both Long and Short trades. Here are the results.

TimeFrame: M5

Total Net Profit: $ 11,435.39

Max DrawDown: ($ 7,994.78)

Number of Trades: 4003

% Wins : 34%

Max Consecutive Losers: 21

RINA Index: -414.86

TimeFrame: M15

Total Net Profit: $ 11,557.05

Max DrawDown: ($ 9,412.90)

Number of Trades: 1171

% Wins : 36%

Max Consecutive Losers: 20

RINA Index: -95.14

[RINA Index should be positive and higher as possible. Rina Index = (Total Net Profit)/((Average DrawDown)x(% Time in the Market))]

I think there are two main disappointing results: 1) the low percentage of winning trades (between 34% and 38% depeding on the timeframe and Case applied); 2) the high number of consecutive losers. With 20 consecutive losers a trader should have iron emotions and lots of patience to not stop trading this system.

By the way, another important factor could be the exit strategy. The strategy exit I used was any of the following:

1) Medium Stoch leaving Overbought/Oversold zone for Long/Short entries;

2) Slow Stoch leaving Overbought/Oversold zone for Long/Short entries;

3) EMA 5 Crossing Below/Above EMA 13 for Long/Short entries;

If someone suggest another exit technique I'll be happy to test it.

Now I will test other pairs namely EURUSD, GBPUSD and USDCHF.

I would love to have your opinions and suggestions.

Thanks,

I am helping to develope a system with a couple friends and I am in need of help and second opinions.

THe issue we have run into is that we want to test our system out using Vhands by Blueruby (thanks man!!)  We are using Multiple Time Frame Stochastics that plot the H4 and D1 and WK1 stochastic 5,3,3 on our H4 charts.  But Vhands is unable to compensate and test this set up.

SO what I am asking for your guys help is do you know what settings I should choose in order to simulate the D1 and WK1 Stochastics on the H4 charts?

I have come up with D1 setting (30, 18, 3) and WK1 setting (150, 90, 3) but I am not sure if this is correct and would like a second or 100th opinion on it.

I found these settings by finding that the 5,3,3 on H4 was taking the last 5 4 hour and last 3 4 hour bars.  So by extension I thought that D1 setting would be taking the last 5 daily and 3 daily bars for the two periods of the MA's.  This then would equal 30 4 hour and 18 4 hour bars, because there are 24 hours in a day and therefor 6 H4 bars in a day, over 5/3 days would be 30/18 H4 bars respectively.

THe same was applied to the weekly.  There are 5 days in the weekly bar and the weekly 5,3,3 setting takes the last 5 and 3 weekly bars.  SO the settings would be 5(30), 3(30), 3 or 150,90,3.

YOu probably dont follow what I am saying but if you can help that would be great.  I just need to be able to plot the daily and weekly stochastic on a H4 chart by changing the setting (x,x,3) of the stochastic.  Thanks

--- 帖子 #1645 ---
sometimes what i do is that for example i have a 15 min chart on and i want a 30 min stochastic setup, i just multiply all the settings by 2 and it ends up being very close to an actual 30 min chart. like rather than 5 3 3 u use 10 6 6 etc....

but if ur using a 1h chart and want 4h setups, u can multiply by 4 but yea it gets kinda too weird to look at and looks all flat and hard to understand so i dont recommend it. the only way it would work is if u zoom out some and then look at it it would look a bit better.

having 2 charts would get u a 4h 8h daily and weekly so i recommend u do that rather than squeezing them all on one chart. trust me.

hope this helps if u wanna know anything else feel free to ask and ill give my opinion.

--- 帖子 #1708 ---
OK, here's a current view of the action from EUR-USD. Two charts, 15min and the next time frame up which (for me) is 1hr.

Notice how the slower moving stochs (15,x,12) & (20,x,12) on the 15 min mirror the movement of the (5,x,3) on the 1 hour.

So, I always know what the 1 hour chart is doing because the slower stochs on the 15 min tell me.

It's the same with other time frames although some behave better than others. I'm still working on 4hr and Daily.

Hope this makes sense.

--- 帖子 #1734 ---
Hi BoxingLife, ElChoco and JD,

A little background, so you know better where I am coming from...

I am principally a mathematician and physicist and so have spent 20 years working with MatLab - the industry standard maths modelling and graphics package. I have long had an interest in digital filters for the markets and have used these to trade futures in the past. But I am brand new to FX. I have my own thread Optimised Trend Trading if you want to see some of the stuff we have done there.

Although I have developed some excellent filters, there was always a missing piece of the jigsaw. The critical information is WHEN/WHEN NOT to trade. The stochs theory I have learned here has just about filled that gap and I am grateful for the generosity and enthusiasm of the good folk on this thread.

I am currently doing some quite advanced modelling of the stochs theory in MatLab, especially looking at frequency and phase responses to optimise the lag times. When Boxing first put up his theory, we were using (50,10,20) and (20,10,0) and (5,3,3) and plotting %K.

Then Melpheos modified this to use (50,2,10) and (20,2,10) and (4,2,2) and plotting %D. This gave an extra bars advance.

I am trying to get a decent analytic theory of how plotting different stochs on one timeframe corresponds to plotting the same stochs on different timeframes. This, I think, is the key to optimising the system but it is not easy because the stoch is a non-linear filter and requires some heavy math. I hope to report results in due course for the benefit of all.

Please can you help me fill in a few gaps here. I have only been with this thread a week (and have only had MetaTrader for 9 days). I am currently learning about the FX markets and learning MT4 and its MQ language at the same time.

I have read:

(a) BoxingLife's original "Sexy Stochastics" PDF

(b) Melpheos' STOCHV PDF

(c) Spud's Elevator 2 Pips PDF

(d) Spud's Stochastic Thread Theory PDF

(e) Quite a bit of this thread.

But I am most interested in some of the trades posted by ElChoco and JD. I am not taking (or even recognising) these trade signals, so clearly I have only part of the story. I started by using 4 different timeframe charts as suggested by Spud with the same stochastic on each (5,3,3) I think it was. Then I moved on to the BoxingLife system which I found much better. Now I have set Melpheos' settings and this seems better still. I am using Boxing's trade rules and have looked at the source code of Melpheos' V Indicator so see his rules in detail.

Please could you advise me if I have missed any of the critical reading material? Even better still, has anyone produced a synthesis summary of the various trading rules to date, so I can check my understanding?

Many thanks

CB.

Codebreaker: Low/High and Exponential. I don't use the %D because the %K seems to "get there quicker" !!

FXGuy: Perfect setup?

1: I'm looking for strong angle and (perhaps) even separation on the slower stochs...
2: ...as the (5,3,3) cuts right back towards or even through them as the price retraces.
3: All three stochs in the next HIGHER time frame are pointing in the right direction (or look as if they are will point in the right direction once the price stops retracing)
4: The (5,3,3) in the next LOWEST time frame is probably in the opposite O/B or O/S area and will be turning around. Also the price in this time frame will probably be hitting the Bollinger Band.All: I never got on with pivot lines, however 10EMA [Edit: did I say 10EMA??? I Meant 6 EMA] and 25EMA and Bollinger Bands on all time frames seems to give TOTALLY AWESOME support and resistance levels. It's an absolutely common occurence for price to halt at (for example) the 10 EMA on the daily chart = 25EMA on the 4Hour chart = Bollnger Band on the 1 Hour chart. When I see confluence like this, chances are the prices aint going anywhere for a while.

Also, chances are that prices WILL reach those lines, especially if there's agreement between multiple time frames. I'm still building my confidence on this one, but it's how I'd like to identify TP levels so I don't get out so quick.

--- 帖子 #1787 ---
Would have to say that this system is still very discretional. Success or failure can be down to how confident the trader is in his position if the price goes against him for a bit.

Some of the best trades have come when i've set the thing going and then had to leave it running. It stops me fiddling, stops me thinking "I ought to take profit now because, look, it's retracing".

I think back testing this would be difficult unless entry and exit rules were made FAR more mechanical. Also, stochs change live. You can't look at a historic chart and think "Yep, I'd definitely have got in there". Depends whether you're a "wait for the candle to close" kind of person. I'm not.

I've looked at systems for over 4 years and refining sexy stochs is turning out to be the most reliable thing I have come across. Perhaps it's also the only one I've REALLY worked at to make it my own.

It's interesting how it ties in with other sytems, guessing the top and bottom is a fools game (or at least i feel like a fool when i try). I never know if we've hit the peak or not. A good Sexy stochs pattern just shows a strong move ALREADY UNDERWAY and then takes a retrace.

This is nothing more than the time-honoured "buy the dips" strategy, just it's so darn visual. You get a great heads-up when the 533 cuts back against the move, and handful of options on how to take the entry.

KUDOS TO US !! Go Team Sexy !!!

Ok, stochsters, here's a quick summary of my use of EMAs etc for defining turning points. This has increased the effectiveness of Sexy Stochs about 10000000% (approx). Hope it's of use to someone.

I add 6EMA, 20EMA and Bollinger band to every time frame.

Here's a series of pics of the action from yesterday on EUR-USD. What I'm looking for is price to hit either of these three indicators on multiple times at the same time!!!

First up is the WEEKLY chart (anyone using this???? haha) Price touches down on the 6EMA of the Weekly. At the same moment, price hits the 20EMA on the Daily chart, AND also touches the first BB of the 4 hour.

When I get confluence like that I can be pretty sure the price isn't going to break down further.

Lo and behold, the 4 hour gives a perfect Sexy Entry going long at exactly the same moment. MMMMMMMMMMmmmmmmmmmmmmmmmmmm.

I know the weekly chart is not on everyone's watch list but the same process occurs on all time frames.  I just saw this one live on friday and thought it was cool.

Enjoy

[BTW: Anyone know how to add text between multiple pictures?]

--- 帖子 #1791 ---
here is a multi time frame example of eurjpy

first of all check out the 4h chart. the gray highlighted area is where the 20 crossed its signal line upward and at the same time the 5 was already above 80. this indicates a strong uptrend.

next we look at the 1h and we see that the 20 is above 80 and the 5 pulled back and touched the 20 line. this is a perfect buy signal on the 1h which is also in sync with the 4h chart makes this trade high probability. no need to hesistate here. we see 4h 20 moving up the 5 above 80 right away we think uptrend then the 1h 20 is above 80 we also think uptrend we just wait for the 5 to cross upward and bam 100+ in a couple of hours.

next

the 4h 20 is above 80 and the 5 is pulling back (blue area). since this means uptrend, we wait for the 1h to tell us when to get in.

so the 4h is looking good.

next we look at the 1h. we see the 20 on the 1h trending down. this trend down is nothing but a pullback of the 5 stoch on the 4h. just like they say a pullback on the daily is a trend change on the lower timeframes. think of it that way.

so we wait for teh 20 to turn back up and we enter on the first signal we get off the 1h which is the area i highlighted in blue

take the time to digest this. it makes pips. trust me

Hmmm....

I'm with ElChoco on this one! I DON'T like the trades where the MED/SLOW stochs are in the OB/OS zones. Far to risky. Like ElChoco, my rule is:

- if the MED/SLOW stochs are trending firmly UP between the 20/80 lines then BUY on the DIPS of the FAST,

- if the MED/SLOW stochs are trending firmly DOWN between the 20/80 then SELL on the PEAKS of the FAST.

OK, there are not so many opportunities but it seems safer to me. And you're all correct in one thing -- sitting looking at the chart waiting for that rare(ish) setup is SOOOO hard!

--- 帖子 #1807 ---
The reason I asked for your rules is that I couldn't see a single EA entry on your chart where I would have got in!!

Can I clarify what you mean here? Let's consider just a long trade. When you say "buy on dips of the fast" do you mean "buy when the fast stoch dips down"? This would tie in more with the arrows on your chart.

My understanding is that the dipping down of the fast stoch just gives a "heads-up" if your trading live and then we enter when the fast stoch turns around and rejoins the direction of the slower stochs.

Therefore, don't go long as the fast stoch dips down but wait until it starts going back up again. I think that would give you a whole different set of signals.

The stochs are just reflecting a retrace of an existing trend. EG, there's a strong move north, price cuts back a little bit, and you jump in long (at a cheaper price) when price returns in the original direction.

I've put some arrows on your chart showing sexy stoch entries that I might have considered. To be honest neither of them are particularly great in hindsight. I would hope that some of the other big price moves that we see on your chart would have shown up on other time frames.

This is only the way that I use Sexy stochs, others may have different ideas. Boxing's last post had me totally confused so I'm still on this.

Also, you might want to consider whether you want the EA to trade the asian session (depending on the currency). You'd probably get loads of silly little entries that eat away at your profits.

Happy code-ing.

OK - after 1800 and something posts we seem to be getting to the crux of this matter. The Team comprise of half a dozen (obviously) very bright guys with international positions in IT, Universities, etc. If we can each look at a simple chart with 3 wavy lines are all interpret that chart in totally different ways, then we have a problem of philosophy.

There is little point in fiddling about optimising stochastic settings, entry and exit points etc until we all agree how the system works!

I think the entry points on my chart for Rule (1) trades are clear. [Rule (2) I am not so sure about as I don't understand it - we need Melpheos to clarify]. When the MED/FAST stochs are heading say NORTH and there is a DIP in the FAST stoch, you BUY. Note that in order to know when the dip has finished and the FAST stoch is heading north again with the others you have to wait until the "V" bottom has fully formed. That is why my signals are LATE compared to the V bottom. But they are still quite good on SOME pairs in SOME timeframes. Same but opposite goes for SHORTS.

But can we please all try to list our understanding of the RULES so we can get a concensus on this. To avoid the ambiguity of language, perhaps the best way is pseudocode, eg:

IF (SLOWstoch heading SOUTH) &&

(MEDstoch heading SOUTH) &&

(FASTstoch < MEDstoch) &&

etc, etc

THEN (SELLsignal = true)

Just take a look at the source code of Melpheos' StochV indicator to see how this is done. Once you have the MT4 basic indicator template, coding the rules is trivially simple and it is obvious (even to a non-coder) what his rules are. Problem is, there are so many of them and some don't seem to work - as Melpheos is the first to admit (Ref. Post 1678)!

Thanks,

CB.

--- 帖子 #1813 ---
Great Start, Codeworker. Wish I could program!

1. I hope Boxing can help in enumerating the rules.

2. From my understanding, there wre are two core ways you can play this strategy. This is within the timeframe, and the secon is with reference to other timeframes.

1. Within the timeframe - lets say we were on M15.

a. The first step would be to consider the position of the 20 and 50 stoch. If 20 and 50 are in overbought zone, i.e., 80+, there is a chance of the uptrend continuing. When the 5 dips down, and then crosses up through its signal line, buy. Therefore, IF 20 and 50 > 80, and %k>%d (if thats the correct terminology for the main/signal line) and %k between 0 and 30 (( this to say that it is not crossing or moving up midway but from the lowest dip)) then BUY. You'll find that when the 5 crosses up from below 20, that is a stronger move.

b. When 20 is above 50 and main line is aboce the signal line ( indicating the two stochs movig up), then the 5 dips down and then crosses up through its signal line, BUY ( per example of 5 above).

Reverse for SELL.

2. MTF. A bit more complex, I think. I'm still studying the charts to determine when to take trades based on trend and countertrend, using higher timeframes for trnd and lower ones for entry. I don't think thinkcountertrends should be ignored, since apart from the pips, these could be signalling reversals.

But, thanks for taking the initiative - I'm sure Boxing/Melpheos and others will help out as well!

Pardy

Guys, I think I have a decent understanding of the entry signal. (Well as good as I can after being exposed to this thread for 24 hours) I am currently back-testing data with the old F12 key and I came across this trade and I am curious to learn how you would have handled it.

[IMG]file:///C:/DOCUME%7E1/RUSSKI%7E1/LOCALS%7E1/Temp/moz-screenshot.jpg[/IMG]

Here is how I viewed this chart. I will attempt to talk through this and give my thoughts here and please feel free to explain how you would have handled this with all your experience.

First off we were in an uptrend approaching the trend line that defined the previous uptrend's bottom. This is the HOUR chart by the way. The fast stoch ticked up after the good size up candle was drawn and consequently gave a (1) signal to buy which kind of surprises me because I would have expected to see a (2) because the 20/50 in over bought territory but whatever, doesn't matter. So first off I placed my stop below the last resistance point. The key here will be will the pair be able to break the TL up or not. Its first attempt would have given a good 10 pips profit so perhaps a portion of the trade could have been taken here but the candle was unable to break though and falls back to a level that now puts us in the red. For the next 3 hours the FAST STOCH reloads for another attempt at this TL. The question is, would it be wise to cut losses and get out and wait for the second signal for another run at it or is it wise to set in this thing and just wait it out?

Had I taken the loss and set out I would have missed the next green candle that was made that creates the FAST STOCH signal to trade on. No sooner does that signal come and there is a full retracement of that candle before there is a final move up and through the trend line. I would very much like to hear how you would handle this trade live with stops/limits/re-entry/etc. Or perhaps you will tell me that with that trend line being so close you would have never taken on this trade to begin with.

If you have any questions regarding of my description above for clarification please ask.

--- 帖子 #1850 ---
It's a bit difficult to see the detail in your chart, but I''ll have a crack at answering your question. I take it we're talking about the trade on the red vertical line?

First up, without looking at other time frames for confirmation, I rarely take trades when the slower stochs are in the "zones of confusion" at the top and bottom of the chart. I've just been burned there too many times.

Also, looking at the chart historicaly, the blue line is already flattening off into a "plateau of doom". Seems the upward energy had already begun to dissipate. Two reasons, then, for me not to consider an entry, although some do. See boxin's last chart.  (Also, quite common to see a spike before a retrace - that might be the last "trade opportunity" you mentioned)

Looking at the same time span on another time frame, you'd probably find a much stronger looking signal. I'd hunt around a bit until you see something that looks 100% likely to be a winner.

Incidentaly, did you take the trade i highlight with the arrow??? Probably the strongest sexy-stoch entry of the move. (It's real easy with hind-sight of course)

Hi Team

I am afraid the inability to code the entry (to say nothing of exit) rules almost drove me mad, so I decided to simplify the whole thing. Attached is a chart of my new indicator. Believe it or not, this IS a stochastic. It has just had some very fancy statistical transformations applied. I call it my "peak hunter". Seems to work on all TF from 5M to 1H, so suits my extreme lack of patience.

The "flawless" trade is like 1 or 6 with the real nice smooth line joining the entry and exit. Trades like 2 are a bit more of a rough ride. Entries 3 and 4 were quickly abandoned at stop for tiny loss.

Trade 6 I took today as I couldn't sleep with thinking about this darned business! Bagged 150 pips. This is more like it!! I am told that I should be happy with 10 to 15 pips a day, but something tells me that we can do better.

Backtesting (F12) indicates successful opportunities 3 days out of 5, so not too bad. And very easy to automate the pinger alert and SMS txt message!

CB.

Please don't ask for details -- this is a work in progress and I see no point in discussing stuff until I am sure it works.

--- 帖子 #1889 ---
I'm not using all TF resistances but when they are obvious i use them. You know everyone has to build his own system in fact.

I think Boxinislife uses only stochastic but i prefer to add peak/valley and resistance/support and a bit of BB but not trend lines.

Someone else will use trendline which also works.

You just have to feel at ease with your strategy. A friend of mine never succeeded with Stochastic (he even blew an account i think but as you can guess, MM was also a big part of the blow up ) but recover like crazy scalping with Kolachi and Linuxtroll.

I tried linuxtroll but i just cant feel this kind of price action and it requires a lot of screentime.

Some people succeed with moving average.

Dont hesitate to go back to demo and focus on your MM. Open an account the size of your real account and try to trade it like it was for real (using stops in function of your maximum risk/trade, limited size lot and limited number of pair - do not use GY, GU or GCHF, those pair are stressfull  )

--- 帖子 #1917 ---
We have all gone through this so don't feel odd or bad in any way. The important thing to do with a demo is to trade it ONLY how you are willing to trade live account. So for example lets say you would never trade a live trade with real cash if you can't set in front of the chart the entire time and watch it, well then don't trade the demo unless you can watch it the entire time.

For me I find that its best to trade a demo according to a written "mechanical" system so that you are reacting to a set of rules when the market moves and not a judgmental bias that you will surely feel as your account goes up and down. IMO, one should have a pre-game plan for every trade before they enter. Stuff like: how long do i want to stay in this trade if there is little to no movement? why am i making this trade and what has history taught me about how quickly i should be in the worlds money.

what I am getting at is when trading stochs you have to really be sensitive to time because if you enter on a stoch signal and there is little to no market reaction to the stoch indicators then be careful how long you stay in the trade because they stochs will roll over on you and go the other way. IMO, keep asking yourself after every new candle closes would i want to take this trade now? if you are not in the worlds money and the answer goes from a YES to a NO get out or seriously look for a price where to exit.

of course these are just my observations and i haven't made a single dime from the FOREX so take anything I say with that in mind.

Was wondering if there's an indicator out there or if one can be made that alerts when all 3 stochs are above or below the middle (50) line. I personally find this as a good filter for taking trades...ie only buy if all stochs are above 50 and sell when all 3 are below 50.

If 20 and 50 stochs are above 50 already, there tend to be good entries when the 5 stoch dips down and crosses over 50 line again.

I've tried using a stoch crossing alert but get too many with the 5 stoch so would be good having a filter that only gives relevant alerts. Also would be good if could set all three variables for each stoch and even decide how many stochs we want to consider (some may only want to use 2)

Anyone else think this would be good?

Different settings will give different signal. 20.2.10/50.2.10 is more reactive than 20.10.10/50.10.10 but might give you more false signal.

You can test with different settings to see which one are the best for you but 20.10.10 is usually very nice in most situations.

--- 帖子 #1939 ---
LOL. I'm a bit of an indicator tart. I attach indicators that look like they could be benificial and now I'm in the process of deciding which ones work for me...this is still a work in progress and there will def be less indicators when I've finished...but thanks for the advice.

Sorry if I didn't make sense...basically when all 3 stochs are above 50 the indicator would give a buy signal and when all 3 are below 50 it would give a sell. As soon as that criteria is me the signal would be given.

eg 2 of the stochs (let's say 20 and 50) are above the middle and as soon as the 5 crosses above from below we get a buy signal. If the 5 moves back below there's no signal because the other 2 are above. But as soon as the 5 (or any 1 of the 3 stochs) moves back up another buy signal is generated.

Have a look at your own charts...this looks like it would give some good signals.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #1950 ---
To be more precise, the SL depends more on the lot size than on the number of pips...

The idea is to keep the risk/trade low but still making enough money.

I started with 5% but now i'm down to 1.5% per trade and i will feel even more at ease with 1%. The bigger the account, the lower risk you can take by trade but making enough money.

So you can have a SL of 50 pips which can be riskier than a 100 pips SL if the risk/trade for the 1st one is 5% while then risk/trade is 2% for the second.

This is a strategy i'm testing right now for one week and a half with 0.1 lots. +2% last week and looking very good this week too (this is on demo account but using very precise rules )

--- 帖子 #1956 ---
Paulus,

This system is rock-solid  I've traded it for months now and it works. One thing that I want to point out is the necessity of checking with the higher timeframes. I know that 60% of the time a setup on the 15m chart looks perfect and works out perfectly. However, it's been mine and others' experiences that checking with the higher timeframes solidifies your trades and almost guarantees your winners. I prefer to trade off the 30m chart and check to make sure it's in sync with the 4hr.  Like Boxing says, why trade off the 15m for a small move when you can chase the bigger moves off the 30m charts. Also, it's easier for a move on the 15m to get turned around than it is for one on the 30m or 1hr.  Kinda like the difference between stopping a bike versus a car or bus   Hope the best for you!

--- 帖子 #1963 ---
If the 20-stoch on the 4hr is pointing down, then if your taking trades off the 30m and the 1h charts, you want to only go short. Pretty much if you find a perfect setup on the 30m/1h charts, then the 5-stoch will be going the right direction because the pullback will have ended and the trend will be resuming.  If you're looking to take trades off the 15m charts, then checking with the 30m and 1h will work. You may not find them going the same direction perfectly but you want to make sure they're not going opposite of what you're wanting to do with the 15m because they will over-rule (in most cases) the 15m setups.

--- 帖子 #1964 ---
Looking at the two charts below you'll see where the yellow vertical line is, I found a nice setup on the 30m chart. Before I placed the trade, I glanced at the 4hr chart and saw the 20 and the 5 stochs supporting the direction of my trade. So I knew i was pretty much good to go.

--- 帖子 #2011 ---
Hi Kimmy,
The trade today on GBPUSD 30min was just after 5.40am BST, need to get up early to catch the worm.
If trading 30min then use 5min for your entry, i.e. look for trend on 4h, signal setup on 30min then enter using 5min.
A cross on the stoch is not confirmed until candle close. (so use 5min to jump ahead)
I don’t agree with JD about 20 being flat as it is well above 80 so will not signal a trend change until it drops below, time of day has more impact, it’s getting late.
Whishing you all the best in your trading.
Terry

--- 帖子 #2038 ---
The first thing I see is that the USDCHF 30 min was on the 2:30 candle meaning 3:00 time of close, when looking at the 5min chart for timing, look at the 2:55 candle for where stoch's are at for it. With this or any other system, I believe in multiple time frame confirmation. The 30 min may be your chart time frame (TF) for trade setup, but i always look to a shorter TF chart for entry as I look to see if there has been any change to the trend.

OK Guys here’s the deal

If you would like to trade this system alongside some fellow traders then there is a trading room that you can join.

Please visit the link below where you will need to download the free software.The room is called Forex and Gold ( should be called The Sexy Room ha ha ......maybe we can change it later ). Once you have your user name and password setup then you need to sign in and you will find the room at Trading Rooms/Trading Rooms/ Community Rooms/ Forex and Gold

http://www.tradingrooms.com/default.aspx

Please have your chart setup as per the Sexy System and have read the thread here (at least the first 20 pages). Any questions about setting the chart up or indicators please keep to the main thread here. Any questions that have already been asked and answered in the main thread ………….then you will be in trouble ………..unless you are looking for clarification about something ofcourse then that is fair enough !

--- 帖子 #2147 ---
Hi ingridk,

This system is one of the first I had experience with when I started forex trading.

"Bringin sexy back" is a type of short-term trend retracement system. The slower stochs determine the trend direction, and the fast stoch (5,3,3) indicates where a retracement (pullback) has occurred in the opposite direction of the trend. After the fast stoch retracement has finished and it starts moving again in the direction of the trend you should enter in that direction with the expectation that the trend will continue. How long or how far is an unknown. This entry method is believed by some to lower the risk on the trade.

This is not a mechanical system, in that some experience with it definitely helps you determine the trades to get into and the ones to avoid. Boxingislife and others have shown many good examples of profitable trades in this thread that you can learn from.

Judgement gained by experience is important with this system. For example, a powerful trend wave may not give you much opportunity to enter on a small pullback - but if you can enter you can sometimes make good profits. On the other hand, a weak trend may offer a perfect setup for entry but may fizzle out without much movement. Keep working with the system and learn gradually and you will get better at seeing the difference.

Wishing you many great trades!

--- 帖子 #2150 ---
Here is a way to avoid some of the bad trades and get into more good ones. It requires that you wait for the right setups -- so you get to improve your dicipline and patience as an added bonus.

Logic: First look at the 4h chart of the pair you want to trade and wait until the slow stochs are oversold -- and both the 50,10,20 and 20,10,20 have crossed the 20 line upward, or the slow stochs are overbought and both the 50,10,20, and 20,10,20 have crossed the 80 line downward.

At that point you start looking for a trade on the 1h chart and simply apply the regular Sexyback rules. The 4h chart gives you the long or short bias you will use to enter trades in the proper direction.

Look at the first chart which is the 4h and notice the zone in between the pink lines. Notice that the slow stochs are in proper relationship and are going from oversold to overbought. This is the zone where I would be looking for long trades on the 1h chart. They don't quite make it to the overbought level, but they cross at the pink line on the right so I wouldn't take any trades after this point. I would start waiting for another ob or os setup on the 4h chart again then.

Ignore all the other lines and stuff on the 4h chart for now.

Ok, look at the 1h chart. Notice the trade entries marked with the turquoise lines and the pips that would have been possible. Very good indeed! It's important to note that trades were only taken in the direction of the stochs on the 4h chart (long). That means there were two other profitable trades skipped during the period in the middle of the chart when the stochs were trending down that couldn't be taken according to this rule. The higher probability trades are with the direction of the longer timeframe.

These four trades would have netted you over 300 pips, safely, in less than a week.

Take a good look at this example and you will understand the basics of making money with this system. All the trades don't work out this well, but a lot of them do. Sexyback is a great system, and this is just a way I have found to improve your probability of making more profitable trades. I hope it works well for you.

Dave

I've always had a warm spot in my heart for this strategy.

The longer I trade the more interested I become in avoiding losses. I don't think you can do that with a screen full of indicators though.

The way I see this system logic is that you are trying to determine the direction of the swing by using the slower stochs and then entering on a pullback. In other words, finding a lower-risk entry point.

The more you can catch a move that is going in the direction of the longer-term trend the more profit you should make and the better your R/R should be overall. The longer term trend is where the money is imho.

--- 帖子 #2170 ---
Hi Lyra, as I explained earlier, you will have more winners and less losers if you are trading with the trend.

There is no way to be sure that you will have a winner when you place a trade with this or any other system. The best you can hope for is to put the odds in your favor. The best way to do that is to trade in the direction that price is tending to go anyway.

When you look at the 4h chart of this pair that I have attached below you will see clearly that the pair has put in a double bottom on June 30 and July 1 then continued on the uptrend it has been on since the middle of March. It looks to me like this was just a retracement to the uptrend line.

The lime colored vertical line is about the time you entered the trade you mention. The gold line is showing a strong uptrend. And the bold violet line drawn across the double bottom is likely to be strong support. Unless this pair trades below that line I would still consider the trend to be up and take only long trades. Also notice that the slow stochs on the 4h are sloping upward which is another good sign here that the trend is still up.

My point is that you should always be aware of the trend at least on the next higher timeframe and it will help you avoid being on the wrong side of a lot of trades.

Hope this helps you to more profitable trades.

pd

--- 帖子 #2214 ---
Hi,

Care to explain the term sling shot?

--- 帖子 #2215 ---
Like a catapult. Pull back on the elastic rubber band and release the projectile.

In this case, the trend is down. That upward retracement is like an elastic band being pulled back waiting to be released. When the 5.3.3 stochs went down and passed 80 level, release the stretched rubber or short the currency.

Cheers

dd4x,

I see on the 15 min a possible slingshot, perhaps this is the next one after your post. I found this set up to be the least risky for me:

I have the 20, 50 and 100 all on the 15 I also have a MTF stochastic for the 5 in magenta on the same window. When the 5 (green) crosses its signal line back, I go in, but only if its in the same direction as the magenta which is the 5 stoch on the 5M, that way I dont get that friggin annoying instant drawdown that sometimes happens as soon as you hit the buy or sell button.

This has me getting about 75% winner or thereabouts. I'm still experimenting with micro lots. One other thing that was not mentioned too much except by Melpheos and by Boxing to me.  Don't get your charts overly cluttered with indicators. Concentrate on reading the stochs and seeing how they respond to price movement.  If you get too many indicators on the charts, you'll get distracted.

ok , lets work a little bit

im sorry i did not write it earlier (after dinner) but i went with my friends to play soccer.

I mostly use 2 settings of sts.

1)4,2,2 and 20,2,10 (got this settings from melpheos, this guy brought here , in this thread a lot of wonderfull job and gave us a lot of good paths)

2)my 2nd settings are :5,3,3 and 35,10,10

right now for me is doesnt matter which i use , i know sts very well and like them a lot.they are easy to use.

When u will use them longer time u will feel same i do

My "strategy" :

i look at 1week and 1Day ; it gives me view of trend (long trend , i very often keep positions during whole day or even week or 2weeks)

I dont use SL and TP (maybe it is not good idea and im not supposed to share this informations but i dont use it)

when i keep positions during whole days , somethimes i have -50p or even -200p and after day or few days i got +200 or +400pips.

But i see on 1week or 1D chart that it will go in my direction.

It makes trading stressless and profitable

for me is important trend! i never trade agains that.

sometimes i dont open new positions day or 2 because i dont see enough good setup.

Dont like to risk and loss. so i keep no trading , but later when i see good setup i got much more pips so it is good recompensate for not trading days

So when i know trend (slow sts are very CLEAR pointing up or down and same is fast sts on 1Week and 1D) im looking for fast sts on 4h and 1h.

and this is my entry.

Very often when i open positions it was retracement , and in hour or a few hours i got -50 or -100pips , i draw fibo on 4h or 1h and check when is hi probably retracement to end , and try to open new position like before.

This gives me 2 times more pips and bigger chance to not get loss.

because if it not drop to make my first positions in profit i will get profit from second positions (it very often recompense loss from 1st positions)

and i can close 1st with small loss and 2nd with bigger profit.

Or if i was right i got profit from both positions [mostly very big profit]

and it is worth risk

uffff i wonder if somebody will read it , hope it is not boring.

sorry for my english , im just polish

if u have more questions just ask i will try to answer.

atachments :

some actuall examples - makret is closed.

1D is clear DOWN , 4h is getting nice setup.
[ i checked 1week and 1month too , there i see : 1month great down trend , and broken up trend on 1week - no need of more confirmations]

i know weekend can bring some changes , but i know it is strond down trend.

i opened sell positions.

even when market will open and i will get -100p I belive it will go down.

sometimes we need to wait to get profit so this is reason i dont use SL and TP.

I close positions when i get profit i like [which is enough for me]

sometimes i trade on 5 pairs.

1st i close with -200p because market went in wrong way and im sure it will not return ,

but 4 other positions i close with +600p or more.

overall im in nice profit

im not afroid to close lossing positions when i see it is nothing i can do with it

but i use high TF it is rare to not be profitable after a few days

i remember pair i had -600p and did not close it , after week i got +300p.

i just opened in wrong time but i was sure it will go where it was poiting to.

Another trade i entered today on EURUSD

i entered slightly late because i was away from my computer, if i had entered on the close of the candle indicated by the yellow arrow i would have hit +30 pips. Still it hit +20 pips and moved my stop loss to breakeven...a free trade.

Success with any strategy, including this one...involves the right psychology. If you follow the rules 100%, you will be in profit. Here is some maths. Say this method had 60% success rate.

(Therefore, hypothetically)

10 Trades

6 x 30 pips = 180 pips

4 x 40 pips = 160 pips

180 -160 pips = 20 pips profit.

with 70% success rate (as it has achieved over this so far this year)

7 x 30 pips = 210 pips

3 x 40 pips = 120 pips

210 - 120 pips = 90 pips profit.

Consistency is in the mind.

--- 帖子 #2321 ---
here is how to do it on metatrader.

1. create one of the stochastic oscillators as normal so that the stochastic window shows at the bottom of your chart.

2. go to navigator -> indicators -> stochastic oscillator

3. click on the button stochastic oscillator and then drag into the first stochastic window

picture attached.

--- 帖子 #2390 ---
Hi lindsayf, thanks for your inquiry and the opportunity to share my view.

although as a sideline I  do watch price action  and was able to determine that an uptrend was in place, from my perspective, the set ups were perfect slingshot set ups. The 20 and 50 were in overbought territory above the 70 level. The correct interpretation of the indicator when it is like this is, that we are now trending very strongly, making these set ups ideal sexy stoch trades. The 20 and 50 lines can remain overbought/sold for a long time during big trends and the slope is not important under these conditions. This interpretation is taught by boxing within the thread and will be confirmed by any experienced stoch watchers. They also showed up with melpheos' alert indicator as scenario 2 valid set ups so Ill rest my case there

P.S I know my case is rested but did I mention 8 out of 8 wins?

--- 帖子 #2395 ---
this was my last trade of the session, I went to bed soon after the entry. price had moved quite a bit during the last two sessions and now needed another breakout above the R2 pivot. I thought that was unlikely on a friday. It was a low probability trade from my perspective

Why did I take a low probability trade?

1. It was a valid set up

2. who am I to call the probability of a set up?

3. I have excellent profits from 8 consequetive wins

4. I can protect my gains using Money Management

5. I  wanted to show the system can lose

6. Trading is not about being right

The losing trade is highlighted in blue. Notice the size of the loss compared to the recent winners. There is no need to be GREEDY, I didnt need any more profit. I didnt like the trade so I only risked a small amount on it. Using money management I was able to overcome FEAR and pull the trigger on a valid set up, knowing it wasnt going to hurt me. Understanding this is more important than any other aspect of trading

I had a lucky run, The market broke out and trended up and I was able to ride it using this trending system. I trade conservatively and safely because I know the market is completely unpredictable and each of those entries could easily have been losers. If so - I would have preserved 95% of my account and been ready for the good times returning. Win or lose, it was good trading and that is all that counts

nah..zip..ahh.. ALL THAT COUNTS!

--- 帖子 #2428 ---
The best advice i give to anyone counting in pips is : count in %age of equity.

For instance i have a trade right now up around 100 pips. One would say, whoa great trade. But if i have taken this trade with a 2% risk and 40 pips SL you can see that my equity is up 5%. If i have taken this trade with 1% risk and 100 pips SL, my equity is up 1%.

But if i have take this trade with 10% and 25 pips SL, my equity is up 40%.

As you can see, the pip count does not mean anything

--- 帖子 #2429 ---
So true.  I put the pips in the post because just saying that I'm up 1% doesn't tell anyone how that trade would've gone for them.  Very good point though.

--- 帖子 #2457 ---
Just a couple quick comments. First, I think Jimmer actually came up with the "slingshot" setup. It was using a longer term sto for "trend", and shorter term to highlite the pullback against that "trend", and visually it looked like a slingshot being pulled back. Buffy uses the same idea, but with a slightly different sto as long term, with 3 short term stos to form "ribbons" (but they give the same visual). And btw, Buffy is a she! lol

You have put together a nice combination, and as you say, just wait for the best setups as there will be plenty to scalp on a daily basis. This approach has the advantage of effectively seeing multiple TFs because of the use of longer term stos combined with short term stos. Having spent several years in Buffys "room", I know there is value in the approach she teaches. Looks like youve applied the theory nicely. I will be taking a close look at what youre doing. Keep up the good work.

Ninja

First, I apologize somewhat for my prior post in that I had just read Boxingislife's initial post and didnt really notice when it occurred. I thought Id share some thoughts on how this approach could be utilized for scalping a steady income daily. Using his tools, and throwing in a couple add'l "trend" tools, I have outlined how one might plan his/her trades each day, and the criteria necessary to take the trades. Ive outlined the criteria on the initial chart, with some add'l observations among the 3 charts.

I would focus solely on these setups, and would typically put on at least a 2lot position, looking to take 1 off and 5 pips, 2nd at 10. If trading a 3lot based position, I would take 1 off at 5, 7, 9or10 as an example. Some might wish to trail on last as early entries may run for a notable distance. I prefer to hit targets, but thats my nature.

With patience to wait for the criteria to be met, I think you will see the potential of this methodology. The 3 charts I have posted only cover about 2 1/2 hrs of trading, so you can imagine what may be possible each day.

--- 帖子 #2459 ---
I mentioned previously that entries might be "tightened" by dropping down in TF. The charts Ive attached show the setup chart as well as a 3 multiple lower TF chart to highlite possible entries. Ive used a short term RSI to highlite these. The explanation is on the low TF chart.

Please understand that Ive made this a bit sensitive on purpose. Personally, this is how I will utilize the slingshot methodology as I like the immediate response time and tightness of entries. If the TFs selected here are a bit "short" for you, simply raise them both by some multiple which better fits you. Of course, likely fewer setups will occur each day, but the ones that do should provide larger moves accordingly. This is the trade-off.

Ive offered this simply as something to try out. Whether you use these specific tools is not important as much as the underlying methodology of essentially selling rallies in a downtrend and buying dips in an uptrend.

Nothing new here, just another way to get there. :-)

As always, comments welcome.

--- 帖子 #2475 ---
My primary trading approach deals with pullbacks following Macd crosses and 1-2-3 setups. I have added Boxingislife's mutliSto to this for add'l setup opportunities. Something I learned with the "slingshot" type setups is that they will often manifest themselves in conjunction with the Macd pulling back after crossing the midline and/or with the pt 3 of a 1-2-3. Thus, its a logical addition to my trading templates. Ive attached a chart of my main TF, and have highlited 3 setups where the methods are nicely confluent with each other. I hope you find the insights beneficial in some way.

By simply adding the Macd to your charts, this crossing may help to alert you of possible setups coming on the multiStos. If you find this of interest, throw it on your charts and look back to see if you find it beneficial. I use an 8/18/8 Macd, but nothing magic here. Try your favorite or just use the standard 12/26/9 for assessing.

The chart Ive attached is actually my low TF (with the Macd/MultiStos). I also have 2 higher TFs (each a 3 multiple higher of the prev). This gives me a nice perspective that approximates a 5min up to nearly a 60min horizon for setups. As Boxingislife stated in his initial post, just wait until you have prime setups, and you can simply ignore the rest! As you can see from my chart, there's no shortage of them. Some will be so-so, some will be beginnings of large trends. With the higher TF setups, you can use the lower TF charts to tighten entries if desired. At some point, you will undoubtedly see a setup on the low TF that starts a move large enough to trigger a setup on the next TF, which may run far enough to trigger a move on the next. Conversely, given a pullback setup on the highest TF, once it starts, a small pullback there may be a setup on the next lower TF, etc. Actually, I know of one of these recently, and I'll add the chart to highlite this for reference.

Good trading

--- 帖子 #2478 ---
Cspip -

Thanks for the kind words. I'll try to address your questions.

Regarding the long term Stos not justifying the long (on that chart), for me they do not. Look at the high TF chart. Those Stos are what I would look for. Green sto (20) above the Red sto (50) with some spread in between them, as well as each sto having a nice spread between its %k (dotted) and %d (solid). I hope you follow.

Its only the 5/3 Sto on the lower TF being used simply because on that TF the pullback has reached OverSold (O/S) at the 20 level. This would tell me that we may be seeing a bounce here (up), which may effectively be the start of the upmove we're trying to catch on the High TF. Follow?

My comment at bottom of chart about 5/3 Sto and Macd - I was merely alluding to the fact that as price was pulling back (Macd pulling back), this had pulled the 5/3 to the oversold level. This wasnt "causing" the setup on the High TF, it was simply a result of it, if you follow.

I did not take this trade, so no actual entry. I tried to highlite some different ways of triggering the entry. This would be up to the trader to use one of these, or perhaps a different method he/she prefers.

I hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #2485 ---
Hopefully, Ive placed my stop where I know the trade has gone wrong, so until it hits it, any movement against me is within my wiggle room.   I normally will give price once to run against me, but not twice.  Once the trade is moving in my favor, I move to BE.  I can always reenter if stop is hit.  My targets tend to fall within a range of 10-20+ pips, so if I get to 5/6 pips in my favor, Im moving my stop.  There are plenty of setups available, and the good ones dont generally cause the problems. I hope this addresses your questions.
